Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
The Twenty Necessary Attributes: Classification and First Two Groups
Sanusi enumerates the first thirteen of the twenty necessary attributes and classifies them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the twenty necessary attributes are classified into essential, negative, attributes of meaning, and moral attributes, and you will be able to list the first thirteen attributes.

Core Idea
The twenty attributes are carefully classified to protect tawhid and negate imperfection.

This passage from Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin presents the authoritative enumeration of divine attributes. Before delving into each attribute, Sanusi gives the overall framework: twenty attributes divided into four categories. In this passage, we learn the first six (essential and negative) and the seven attributes of meaning. The remaining seven moral attributes are mentioned but not listed here.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very concise style, typical of matn works.
2
Identify the three groups
The passage presents six attributes, then seven attributes of meaning, then mentions seven moral attributes. Find each group and notice how Sanusi defines or explains key terms.
3
Understand the classification
The first attribute (Existence) is essential (nafsī), meaning it is inherent to God's essence. The next five are negative (salbiyya), denying imperfections. The attributes of meaning are positive attributes that subsist in the essence.
The negative attributes do not deny God's perfection; they deny imperfections.
4
Reflect on the incomplete list
The passage ends with 'seven attributes called moral attributes' without listing them. This is a deliberate gap; future lessons will complete the list. For now, focus on the structure.
The moral attributes are derived from the attributes of meaning (e.g., 'Powerful' from Power).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَمِمَّا يَجِبُ لِمَوْلانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ : عِشْرُونَ صِفَةً . الصِّفَاتُ الْوَاجِبَةُ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى : وَهِيَ : الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْقِدَمُ ، وَالْبَقَاءُ ، وَمُخَالَفَتُهُ تَعَالَى لِلْحَوَادِثِ ، وَقِيَامُهُ تَعَالَى بِنَفْسِهِ ؛ أَيْ : لا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى مَحَلٍّ وَلا مُخَصِّصٍ ، وَالْوَحْدَانِيَّةُ ؛ أَيْ : لا ثَانِيَ لَهُ فِي ذَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي صِفَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي أَفْعَالِهِ . فَهَذِهِ سِتُّ صِفَاتٍ ، الأُولَى نَفْسِيَّةٌ وَهِيَ الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبِيَّةٌ . ثُمَّ يَجِبُ لَهُ تَعَالَى سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتُ الْمَعَانِي وَهِيَ الْقُدْرَةُ وَالْإِرَادَةُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَتَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَالْعِلْمُ الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِجَمِيعِ الْوَاجِبَاتِ وَالْجَائِزَاتِ وَالْمُسْتَحِيلاتِ وَالْحَيَاةُ وَهِيَ لا تَتَعَلَّقُ بِشَيْءٍ . وَالسَّمْعُ وَالْبَصَرُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ وَالْكَلامُ الَّذِي لَيْسَ بِحَرْفٍ وَلا صَوْتٍ وَيَتَعَلَّقُ بِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ الْعِلْمُ مِنَ الْمُتَعَلَّقَاتِ . ثُمَّ سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتٌ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ .
Then among what is necessary for our Master, Majestic and Mighty, are twenty attributes. The attributes necessary for God Most High are: Existence, Eternity, Everlastingness, His being unlike originated things, His self-subsistence—meaning He does not depend on a locus or a specifier—and Oneness—meaning there is no second to Him in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His acts. These are six attributes: the first is essential (nafsī), which is Existence, and the five after it are negative (salbiyya). Then there are necessary for Him seven attributes called the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī): Power and Will, which relate to all possible things; Knowledge, which relates to all necessary, possible, and impossible things; Life, which does not relate to anything; Hearing and Sight, which relate to all existent things; and Speech, which is not a letter or a sound, and relates to what knowledge relates to of the relata. Then seven attributes called moral attributes (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya).
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and classification of the twenty attributes that are necessary for God. It begins by stating that twenty attributes are necessary. It then lists the first six: Existence (wujūd), Eternity (qidam), Everlastingness (baqā'), Being unlike originated things (mukhālafatuhu li-l-ḥawādith), Self-subsistence (qiyāmuhu bi-nafsihi, explained as not needing a place or a specifier), and Oneness (waḥdāniyya, explained as having no second in essence, attributes, or actions). After the list, it classifies these six: the first (Existence) is essential (nafsī), meaning it is inherent to the essence; the remaining five are negative (salbiyya), meaning they deny imperfections from God. Next, it introduces the seven attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī), which are positive attributes that subsist in the essence: Power (qudra) and Will (irāda), both relating to all possible things; Knowledge (‘ilm), relating to all necessary, possible, and impossible things; Life (ḥayāt), which does not relate to anything; Hearing (sam‘) and Sight (baṣar), relating to all existents; and Speech (kalām), which is not composed of letters or sounds and relates to the same objects as knowledge. Finally, it mentions the seven moral attributes (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya) but does not list them in this passage (they are likely the same as the ma‘nawiyya inferred from the ma‘ānī, such as being powerful, willing, etc.). The list is incomplete, but the structure is clear: total of twenty, divided into three groups.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The negative attributes (like qidam and baqā') deny God's perfection.
Correction: The negative attributes do not deny God's perfection; they deny imperfections such as origination or annihilation.

Checkpoint
How many of the twenty necessary attributes are classified as 'negative' (salbiyya) in this passage?
A) Six
B) Five
C) Seven
D) One

Key Takeaway
The twenty necessary attributes are divided into four categories: essential, negative, attributes of meaning, and moral attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that God's speech (الكلام) is not letters or sounds. When you recite the Qur'an, are you conscious that you are engaging with a reality beyond physical words? How will this change the way you approach your next recitation from this moment forward? Commit to one action that reminds you of this truth.
?
The attributes of meanings (القدرة، الإرادة، etc.) are said to be eternal and subsisting in God's essence. If God's knowledge encompasses all things—even your secret thoughts—how does that make you feel in this very moment? What will you do differently today knowing that He knows you completely?
?
Oneness (الوحدانية) means no second in essence, attributes, or actions. In the hidden depths of your heart, do you ever fear anyone besides God or rely on anyone else as the ultimate cause? Identify one area of your life where you struggle with this and make a firm intention to purify your tawhid in that area starting now.

Divine Attributes

5 min
The Six Foundational Attributes
Sanusi lists the first six necessary attributes and classifies them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first six necessary attributes of Allah, including the self-necessary attribute of existence and the five negative attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's necessary attributes begin with existence and five negations.

Sanusi starts by listing the foundational attributes. He mentions six: existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, dissimilarity, self-subsistence, and uniqueness. The first is self-necessary, while the rest are negative, restricting what Allah cannot be. This classification helps us understand that some attributes affirm divine perfection while others negate imperfection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the list of six attributes and how Sanusi defines 'self-subsistence' and 'uniqueness'.
The definitions are given in parentheses.
2
Identify the six attributes
Write down the six attributes: existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, dissimilarity, self-subsistence, and uniqueness. Understand what each means from the passage.
Existence is self-necessary; the others negate restrictions.
3
Distinguish self-necessary from negative
Sanusi states that the first attribute (existence) is self-necessary (nafsiyya), and the remaining five are negative (salbiyya). Reflect on why existence is considered self-necessary and why the others negate attributes of creation.
Negative attributes do not describe what Allah is, but what He is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفات الواجبةُ اللهِ تعالى وَهِيَ : الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْقِدَمُ ، وَالْبَقَاءُ ، وَمُخَالَفَتُهُ تَعَالَى لِلْحَوَادِثِ ، وَقِيَامُهُ تَعَالَى بِنَفْسِهِ ؛ أَي : لا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى مَحَلٌّ ، وَلا مُخَصِّص ، وَالْوَحْدَانِيَّةُ ؛ أَيْ : لَا ثَانِيَ لَهُ فِي ذَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي صِفَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي أَفْعَالِهِ . فَهَذِهِ سِتْ صِفَاتِ ، الأُولَى نَفْسِيَّةٌ ؛ وَهِيَ الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبِيَّةٌ ثُمَّ يَجِبُ لَهُ تَعَالَى سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتِ الْمَعَانِي وَهِيَ الْقُدْرَةُ وَالْإِرَادَةُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَتَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَالْعِلْمُ الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِجَمِيعِ الْوَاجِبَاتِ وَالْجَائِزَاتِ وَالْمُسْتَحِيلات وَالْحَيَاةُ ، وَهِيَ لا تَتَعَلَّقُ بِشَيْءٍ . وَالسَّمْعُ وَالْبَصَرُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ وَالْكَلامُ الَّذِي لَيْسَ بِحَرْفٍ وَلا صَوْتٍ ، وَيَتَعَلَّقُ بِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ الْعِلْمُ مِنَ الْمُتَعَلَّقَاتِ ثُمَّ سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتٍ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ ، وَهِيَ مُلازِمَةٌ لِلسَّبْعِ الْأُولَى وَهِيَ كَوْنُهُ تَعَالَى قَادِراً ، وَمُرِيداً ، وَعَالِماً ، وَحَيَّاً ، وَسَمِيعاً ، وَبَصِيراً ، وَمُتَكَلِّماً
The necessary attributes of Allah, may He be exalted, are: existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, His being unlike originated things, His being self-subsisting, i.e., He does not need a locus nor a specifier, and uniqueness, i.e., there is no second to Him in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His acts. So these are six attributes: the first is self-necessary, which is existence, and the five after it are negative. Then there must be for Him, may He be exalted, seven attributes called attributes of meaning: power and will, both related to all possible things; knowledge, related to all necessary, contingent, and impossible things; life, which is not related to anything; hearing and seeing, related to all existent things; and speech, which is not with a letter or a sound, and it relates to what knowledge relates to of the things related. Then seven attributes called attributes of meaning-with-signification, and they are necessary concomitants of the first seven, and they are: His being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage enumerates the twenty necessary attributes of Allah. It first lists six attributes: existence (al-wujūd), pre-eternity (al-qidam), everlastingness (al-baqā'), dissimilarity to originated things (mukhālafatuhu lil-ḥawādith), self-subsistence (qiyāmuhu bi-nafsihi), and uniqueness (al-waḥdāniyya). The author then explains that the first, existence, is a self-attribute (nafsiyya), while the remaining five are negative (salbiyya) because they negate what is incompatible with divinity. Next, the author introduces seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī): power (al-qudra), will (al-irāda), knowledge (al-‘ilm), life (al-ḥayāh), hearing (as-sam‘), seeing (al-baṣar), and speech (al-kalām). Each has a specific scope: power and will relate to all possible things; knowledge encompasses necessary, contingent, and impossible; life does not relate to any object; hearing and seeing relate to all existents; and speech, unlike human speech, is not composed of letters or sounds and relates to the same objects as knowledge. Finally, the author lists seven attributes of meaning-with-signification (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya), which are necessary concomitants (mulāzima) of the attributes of meaning: being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking. These are the states or relational aspects that necessarily follow from the existence of the attributes of meaning in God. In total, there are twenty necessary attributes: six initial, seven of meaning, and seven of meaning-with-signification.

الصفات السلبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Negative attributes are not real attributes or are unimportant.
Correction: The passage includes five negative attributes as necessary for Allah. They are real attributes in the sense that they are essential descriptions of what Allah must not be, and they are part of the twenty necessary attributes.

Checkpoint
How many of the six foundational attributes are classified as negative (salbiyya)?
A) One
B) Five
C) Six
D) None

Key Takeaway
Allah's necessary attributes include existence (self-necessary) and five negative attributes that negate imperfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The source says Allah is unlike anything originated. Is there any mental image or conception of Allah that I hold which actually resembles created things? What must I do to purify my belief?
?
Allah is self-subsisting—He needs no place or specifier. Do I subconsciously rely on any created thing as if it were indispensable for my existence or happiness? In what area of my life must I reaffirm total reliance on Allah alone?
?
Uniqueness means no second in essence, attributes, or acts. Have I ever, even momentarily, attributed power or control to someone or something as if it were independent of Allah? How will I guard my heart against hidden shirk today?

Divine Attributes

The Seven Attributes of Meaning
Sanusi enumerates the seven attributes of meaning and their scopes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven attributes of meaning: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, seeing, and speech, and their respective scopes of relation.

Core Idea
Allah's perfection is realized through seven substantive attributes of meaning.

After the negative attributes, Sanusi introduces seven attributes that affirm positive divine qualities. These are power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, seeing, and speech. Each relates to specific categories of objects, and the passage details these scopes. This lesson explores their meanings and how they differ from human attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on attributes of meaning
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the list and the descriptions that follow each attribute.
The passage uses 'tuta‘allaq' (related to) to specify scope.
2
Identify and memorize the seven
Write down the seven attributes: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, seeing, speech. Notice that life is said to be 'not related to anything'.
Life is a necessary condition for other attributes but has no object.
3
Understand the scopes of relation
For each attribute, note what it relates to. Power and will relate to all possible things; knowledge relates to all necessary, contingent, and impossible things; hearing and seeing relate to all existent things; speech relates to the same objects as knowledge.
Speech is described as not composed of letters or sounds, emphasizing its perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفات الواجبةُ اللهِ تعالى وَهِيَ : الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْقِدَمُ ، وَالْبَقَاءُ ، وَمُخَالَفَتُهُ تَعَالَى لِلْحَوَادِثِ ، وَقِيَامُهُ تَعَالَى بِنَفْسِهِ ؛ أَي : لا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى مَحَلٌّ ، وَلا مُخَصِّص ، وَالْوَحْدَانِيَّةُ ؛ أَيْ : لَا ثَانِيَ لَهُ فِي ذَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي صِفَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي أَفْعَالِهِ . فَهَذِهِ سِتْ صِفَاتِ ، الأُولَى نَفْسِيَّةٌ ؛ وَهِيَ الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبِيَّةٌ ثُمَّ يَجِبُ لَهُ تَعَالَى سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتِ الْمَعَانِي وَهِيَ الْقُدْرَةُ وَالْإِرَادَةُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَتَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَالْعِلْمُ الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِجَمِيعِ الْوَاجِبَاتِ وَالْجَائِزَاتِ وَالْمُسْتَحِيلات وَالْحَيَاةُ ، وَهِيَ لا تَتَعَلَّقُ بِشَيْءٍ . وَالسَّمْعُ وَالْبَصَرُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ وَالْكَلامُ الَّذِي لَيْسَ بِحَرْفٍ وَلا صَوْتٍ ، وَيَتَعَلَّقُ بِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ الْعِلْمُ مِنَ الْمُتَعَلَّقَاتِ ثُمَّ سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتٍ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ ، وَهِيَ مُلازِمَةٌ لِلسَّبْعِ الْأُولَى وَهِيَ كَوْنُهُ تَعَالَى قَادِراً ، وَمُرِيداً ، وَعَالِماً ، وَحَيَّاً ، وَسَمِيعاً ، وَبَصِيراً ، وَمُتَكَلِّماً
The necessary attributes of Allah, may He be exalted, are: existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, His being unlike originated things, His being self-subsisting, i.e., He does not need a locus nor a specifier, and uniqueness, i.e., there is no second to Him in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His acts. So these are six attributes: the first is self-necessary, which is existence, and the five after it are negative. Then there must be for Him, may He be exalted, seven attributes called attributes of meaning: power and will, both related to all possible things; knowledge, related to all necessary, contingent, and impossible things; life, which is not related to anything; hearing and seeing, related to all existent things; and speech, which is not with a letter or a sound, and it relates to what knowledge relates to of the things related. Then seven attributes called attributes of meaning-with-signification, and they are necessary concomitants of the first seven, and they are: His being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage enumerates the twenty necessary attributes of Allah. It first lists six attributes: existence (al-wujūd), pre-eternity (al-qidam), everlastingness (al-baqā'), dissimilarity to originated things (mukhālafatuhu lil-ḥawādith), self-subsistence (qiyāmuhu bi-nafsihi), and uniqueness (al-waḥdāniyya). The author then explains that the first, existence, is a self-attribute (nafsiyya), while the remaining five are negative (salbiyya) because they negate what is incompatible with divinity. Next, the author introduces seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī): power (al-qudra), will (al-irāda), knowledge (al-‘ilm), life (al-ḥayāh), hearing (as-sam‘), seeing (al-baṣar), and speech (al-kalām). Each has a specific scope: power and will relate to all possible things; knowledge encompasses necessary, contingent, and impossible; life does not relate to any object; hearing and seeing relate to all existents; and speech, unlike human speech, is not composed of letters or sounds and relates to the same objects as knowledge. Finally, the author lists seven attributes of meaning-with-signification (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya), which are necessary concomitants (mulāzima) of the attributes of meaning: being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking. These are the states or relational aspects that necessarily follow from the existence of the attributes of meaning in God. In total, there are twenty necessary attributes: six initial, seven of meaning, and seven of meaning-with-signification.

Checkpoint
Which attribute of meaning does NOT relate to any object?
A) Power
B) Life
C) Speech
D) Knowledge

Key Takeaway
The seven attributes of meaning are positive divine qualities, each with a specific scope, affirming Allah's perfection in power, knowledge, and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that Allah's hearing and seeing encompass every existent thing, what would you do differently if you truly believed that He sees and hears even your silent thoughts and secret actions? Will you begin today by monitoring your inner state as if He is watching?
?
If Allah's speech is not like human speech, how should that transform your relationship with the Quran? When you recite the Quran, do you treat it as a mere book or as the very attribute of the All-Mighty? Commit to reciting one verse with the awareness that you are engaging with His eternal speech.
?
The attribute of life in Allah is a condition for all other attributes—He is the Living who never dies. How does your own awareness of your mortality affect your urgency in obeying the Living One? What is one thing you will do today to prepare for your meeting with Him?

beginner
5 min
The Seven Attributes of Meaning-with-Signification
Sanusi lists the seven attributes of meaning-with-signification as necessary concomitants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven attributes of meaning-with-signification (ma‘nawiyya) and how they necessarily follow from the attributes of meaning.

Core Idea
Allah's being 'powerful, willing, knowing, etc.' are necessary states that accompany the attributes of meaning.

The final set of seven attributes are called 'meaning-with-signification' (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya). They are not separate qualities but are the necessary consequences of having the attributes of meaning. For example, if Allah has power (attribute of meaning), then He is necessarily powerful (attribute of meaning-with-signification). This lesson clarifies their relationship and completes the total of twenty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on attributes of meaning-with-signification
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how each attribute of meaning-with-signification corresponds to an attribute of meaning.
The passage says they are 'mulāzima' (necessary concomitants) of the first seven.
2
Identify the seven concomitants
List the seven: being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking. Match each to an attribute of meaning.
These are states or relational descriptions.
3
Understand why they are necessary
Reflect that if an attribute of meaning exists in Allah, then the description of being 'powerful' etc. is necessarily true. They are not additional independent attributes.
This distinguishes them from attributes of meaning which are substantive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصفات الواجبةُ اللهِ تعالى وَهِيَ : الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْقِدَمُ ، وَالْبَقَاءُ ، وَمُخَالَفَتُهُ تَعَالَى لِلْحَوَادِثِ ، وَقِيَامُهُ تَعَالَى بِنَفْسِهِ ؛ أَي : لا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى مَحَلٌّ ، وَلا مُخَصِّص ، وَالْوَحْدَانِيَّةُ ؛ أَيْ : لَا ثَانِيَ لَهُ فِي ذَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي صِفَاتِهِ ، وَلا فِي أَفْعَالِهِ . فَهَذِهِ سِتْ صِفَاتِ ، الأُولَى نَفْسِيَّةٌ ؛ وَهِيَ الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبِيَّةٌ ثُمَّ يَجِبُ لَهُ تَعَالَى سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتِ الْمَعَانِي وَهِيَ الْقُدْرَةُ وَالْإِرَادَةُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَتَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَالْعِلْمُ الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِجَمِيعِ الْوَاجِبَاتِ وَالْجَائِزَاتِ وَالْمُسْتَحِيلات وَالْحَيَاةُ ، وَهِيَ لا تَتَعَلَّقُ بِشَيْءٍ . وَالسَّمْعُ وَالْبَصَرُ الْمُتَعَلِّقَانِ بِجَمِيعِ الْمَوْجُودَاتِ وَالْكَلامُ الَّذِي لَيْسَ بِحَرْفٍ وَلا صَوْتٍ ، وَيَتَعَلَّقُ بِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ الْعِلْمُ مِنَ الْمُتَعَلَّقَاتِ ثُمَّ سَبْعُ صِفَاتٍ تُسَمَّى : صِفَاتٍ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ ، وَهِيَ مُلازِمَةٌ لِلسَّبْعِ الْأُولَى وَهِيَ كَوْنُهُ تَعَالَى قَادِراً ، وَمُرِيداً ، وَعَالِماً ، وَحَيَّاً ، وَسَمِيعاً ، وَبَصِيراً ، وَمُتَكَلِّماً
The necessary attributes of Allah, may He be exalted, are: existence, pre-eternity, everlastingness, His being unlike originated things, His being self-subsisting, i.e., He does not need a locus nor a specifier, and uniqueness, i.e., there is no second to Him in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His acts. So these are six attributes: the first is self-necessary, which is existence, and the five after it are negative. Then there must be for Him, may He be exalted, seven attributes called attributes of meaning: power and will, both related to all possible things; knowledge, related to all necessary, contingent, and impossible things; life, which is not related to anything; hearing and seeing, related to all existent things; and speech, which is not with a letter or a sound, and it relates to what knowledge relates to of the things related. Then seven attributes called attributes of meaning-with-signification, and they are necessary concomitants of the first seven, and they are: His being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage enumerates the twenty necessary attributes of Allah. It first lists six attributes: existence (al-wujūd), pre-eternity (al-qidam), everlastingness (al-baqā'), dissimilarity to originated things (mukhālafatuhu lil-ḥawādith), self-subsistence (qiyāmuhu bi-nafsihi), and uniqueness (al-waḥdāniyya). The author then explains that the first, existence, is a self-attribute (nafsiyya), while the remaining five are negative (salbiyya) because they negate what is incompatible with divinity. Next, the author introduces seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī): power (al-qudra), will (al-irāda), knowledge (al-‘ilm), life (al-ḥayāh), hearing (as-sam‘), seeing (al-baṣar), and speech (al-kalām). Each has a specific scope: power and will relate to all possible things; knowledge encompasses necessary, contingent, and impossible; life does not relate to any object; hearing and seeing relate to all existents; and speech, unlike human speech, is not composed of letters or sounds and relates to the same objects as knowledge. Finally, the author lists seven attributes of meaning-with-signification (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya), which are necessary concomitants (mulāzima) of the attributes of meaning: being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking. These are the states or relational aspects that necessarily follow from the existence of the attributes of meaning in God. In total, there are twenty necessary attributes: six initial, seven of meaning, and seven of meaning-with-signification.

بصيراً
متكلماً

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Attributes of meaning-with-signification are separate, independent attributes adding to the divine essence.
Correction: They are necessary descriptions entailed by the attributes of meaning, not additional essences. The text says they are 'mulāzima' (necessary concomitants), not separate attributes.

Checkpoint
How are the seven attributes of meaning-with-signification related to the seven attributes of meaning?
A) They are completely independent
B) They are necessary concomitants
C) They are negations
D) They are identical

Key Takeaway
The seven attributes of meaning-with-signification are the necessary states that follow from the attributes of meaning, completing the twenty necessary attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
As you read that Allah is 'knowing, willing, powerful...' do you realize that these are not just names but necessary truths about your Creator? How would your life change if you truly believed that He knows every thought you think, wills every event, and has power over everything? Take a moment to recite these seven attributes with conviction, and ask yourself: Am I living as if I truly believe this?
?
The attribute 'speaking' means Allah speaks. When was the last time you read His speech, the Qur'an, as if He were personally addressing you? Today, choose one verse and listen to it as Allah's direct command to you. What is He telling you to do?
?
If Allah is 'seeing' and 'hearing' every detail of your life — even what you hide in your heart — then you are never alone and never hidden. Does this thought bring you comfort or fear? Commit to living the next hour aware that He sees and hears everything. How will that change your actions?

The Seven Attributes of Meaning
Enumerates the seven attributes of meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya) and their relationship to the essential attributes of God in Ash‘ari theology.

Core Idea
The seven attributes of meaning are necessary concomitants of God's essential attributes.

Sanusi now moves from the essential attributes to the attributes of meaning. These seven attributes logically follow from the first seven and describe how God's essence is qualified in relation to His actions. This passage lists them concisely, providing the basis for understanding God's power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, and speech as real and eternal attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal translation. Notice the two parts: the statement of concomitance and the list of seven attributes.
The Arabic uses 'كونه تعالى' meaning 'that He, exalted, is...'.
2
Understand 'concomitant'
Reflect on the phrase 'ملازمة للسبع الأولى' (concomitant with the first seven). What does it mean for an attribute to be concomitant with another?
Concomitant here means logically necessary and inseparable.
3
List the seven attributes
Identify each of the seven attributes: powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, speaking. Write them in Arabic and English.
These are the ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya.
4
Reflect on their significance
Ask yourself why these attributes are called 'of meaning'. How do they relate to God's essence?
They are real attributes subsisting in the essence, not separate entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَهِيَ مُلازِمَةٌ لِلسَّبْعِ الْأُولَى. وَهِيَ كَوْنُهُ تَعَالَى قَادِراً، وَمُرِيداً، وَعَالِماً، وَحَيَّاً، وَسَمِيعاً، وَبَصِيراً، وَمُتَكَلِّماً.
And they are concomitant with the first seven. And they are that He, exalted, is powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a brief enumeration of the seven attributes of meaning (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya) in the Ash‘ari tradition. The phrase 'concomitant with the first seven' refers to the seven essential attributes (wujūd, qidam, baqā’, mukhālafa li-l-ḥawādith, qiyām bi-nafsih, waḥdāniyya) already established. The seven attributes listed—power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech—are called 'of meaning' because they are rooted in the divine essence and are known through rational inference. Each is a necessary (wājib) attribute of God, meaning its opposite is impossible. The list is standard in Ash‘ari theology, and these attributes are the basis for understanding God's actions and His relationship to creation.

Correction: In Ash‘ari theology, they are not separate entities but real attributes subsisting in the essence without being identical to it.

The Possible Attribute of God's Actions
Defines the sole possible attribute regarding God's actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the possible (jā'iz) attribute for God's actions and its significance for divine free will.

Core Idea
God’s possible actions are voluntary, not compulsory.

In Ash‘ari theology, attributes of God are divided into necessary, impossible, and possible. This lesson focuses on the possible: the sphere of God's free choice. The passage defines it succinctly: God may either do or leave any possible thing. Let's explore what this means.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic sentence once without analysis. Let its wording sink in.
Notice the key terms: جائز, فعل, ترك, ممكن.
2
Understand 'jā'iz' in context
This term means 'possible' or 'permissible'. In this context, it describes what God may freely do or not do.
3
Reflect on divine freedom
The definition shows that God's actions are not necessitated. He has full choice to act or abstain.
This affirms Ash‘ari belief in God's absolute free will.
4
Address a common misunderstanding
Some think 'possible' implies imperfection in God. Actually, it highlights His autonomy—nothing compels Him.
See the misconception in the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْجَائِزُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَىٰ فَفِعْلُ كُلِّ مُمْكِنٍ أَوْ تَرْكُهُ
And as for the possible regarding Him, exalted: it is the doing of every possible thing or leaving it.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a brief definition of the category of the possible (jā’iz) in relation to God. In Ash‘ari theology, attributes are divided into necessary (wājib), impossible (mustaḥīl), and possible (jā’iz). For God, the only possible is in the sphere of His actions: He may either create or not create any possible thing. This affirms His absolute free will (irāda) and power (qudra)—nothing compels Him to act, and He is not subject to any external cause or obligation. This one-sentence definition succinctly captures the Ash‘ari stance on divine freedom.

Key Terms

ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'possible' means God could be imperfect; rather, it means His actions are not necessitated—He does what He wills.
Correction: The 'possible' attribute does not imply any imperfection; it underscores God's absolute autonomy.

Checkpoint

A) God cannot leave any action undone.
B) God must create the world.
C) God can either do or leave any possible thing.
D) God's actions are determined by His nature.

Key Takeaway
God's possible actions are those He may freely do or leave.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Do you ever act as if God is obligated to answer your prayers or meet your expectations? This passage says He may do or leave any possible thing. Will you repent of any sense of entitlement and submit fully to His free will?

The Possible in Allah's Action (Al-Ja'iz)
Sanusi defines the possible attribute for Allah as doing or leaving any possible thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's action is characterized by absolute freedom — He may do or leave any possible thing, unconstrained by external necessity.

Core Idea
Allah's action is possible, not necessary — He freely does or leaves every possible thing.

In this lesson, we explore the third category of divine attributes: the possible (al-jā'iz). After establishing the necessary and the impossible, Sanusi now defines the scope of Allah's free choice. This brief but profound statement affirms that nothing compels Allah to act or refrain — His will is sovereign over all possible things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic definition and its translation. Notice its concise structure and the inclusion of both doing and leaving.
The passage is very short but packs a lot of meaning.
2
Understand 'jā'iz'
The term jā'iz refers to what is permissible or possible — not obligatory or impossible. It is the middle category between wājib and mustaḥīl.
This term is central to Ash'ari theology.
3
Grasp the scope
The definition covers both doing and leaving 'every possible thing'. This means Allah has complete freedom to create or not create, to act or refrain.
The phrase 'kulli mumkin' emphasizes universality.
4
Reflect on implications
This refutes any notion that Allah is compelled to act. His will is absolutely free, and nothing in creation can force His hand.
This is a key difference from some philosophical views.
5
Connect to kalam framework
This completes the threefold classification for divine actions: necessary, impossible, and possible. Understanding this classification is fundamental to Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الْجَائِزُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَىٰ فَفِعْلُ كُلِّ مُمْكِنٍ أَوْ تَرْكُهُ
And as for the possible with respect to Him, exalted, it is the doing of every possible thing or leaving it.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This is a brief definition of the category of the possible (jāʾiz) in relation to Allah. It states that the possible in His right is simply that He may do any possible thing or leave it undone. This affirms Allah's absolute freedom and power, unconstrained by any external necessity.

Key Terms
جائز
ممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The belief that Allah is compelled to create or to do certain things, as if He has no choice.
Correction: Sanusi affirms that Allah's action is purely possible: He may do or leave any possible thing. This refutes any notion of external compulsion or necessity on Allah.

?

Proof of Allah's Eternity (Qidam)
Sanusi proves Allah's eternity using the impossibility of circularity or infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that Allah must be eternal, based on the impossibility of circularity or infinite regress.

Core Idea
Allah's eternity is proven by the absurdity of an endless chain of causes.

Sanusi presents a concise but powerful proof for the necessity of Allah's eternity. The reasoning is simple: if Allah were not eternal, He would need a creator, and that creator would need a creator, leading to an impossible chain. This short passage establishes a cornerstone of Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Understand the starting point
Recognize the conditional: if Allah were not eternal, He would be originated (ḥādith). This sets up the proof by contradiction.
An originated thing is something that comes into existence after not existing.
2
Identify the implication
An originated being depends on an originator (muḥdith). So Allah would need an external cause.
3
Grasp the two impossibilities
The originator itself must be either eternal or originated. If eternal, we have circularity (dawr); if originated, we have an infinite regress (tasalsul). Both are rationally impossible.
Circularity means A depends on B and B depends on A. Infinite regress means an endless chain of causes.
4
Conclude the proof
Since circularity and infinite regress are impossible, the original assumption that Allah is not eternal must be false. Therefore, Allah is necessarily eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْقِدَم لَهُ تَعَالَى : فَلَأَنَّهُ لَوْ لَمْ يَكُنْ قَدِيماً لَكَانَ حَادِثاً ، فَيَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى مُحْدِثٍ ، وَيَلْزَمُ الدَّوْرُ أَوِ التَّسَلْسُلُ .
And as for the proof of the necessity of eternity for Him, exalted: because if He were not eternal, He would be originated, and thus would depend on an originator, and that would lead to circularity or infinite regress.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This is a proof that Allah must be eternal (qadīm). It argues that if He were not eternal, He would be originated (ḥādith), and thus would need an originator. That originator would also need an originator, leading to either circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul), both of which are impossible. Therefore, Allah must be eternal.

Key Terms
وجوب القدم
قديم
حادث
دور
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah could be originated but have an external originator; the argument shows that would lead to absurdities.
Correction: If Allah were originated, He would need an originator, and that originator would need an originator, leading to circularity or infinite regress—both impossible. Therefore, Allah cannot be originated; He must be eternal.

Checkpoint
What would happen if Allah were not eternal?
A) He would be self-sufficient
B) He would depend on an originator, leading to circularity or infinite regress
C) He would be greater
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Allah's eternity is proven by the absurdity of an endless regress or circular dependency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah were not eternal, He would need an originator. Do you sometimes live as if you are self-sufficient, forgetting that you are originated and depend on Allah every single moment? How can you make that dependence real in your daily actions?
?
The proof shows that anything originated must have an originator. Your own existence is originated. Are you truly relying on the Eternal One alone, or do you seek ultimate security from created things that themselves fade?
?
Imagine your life's foundation rested on an infinite chain of causes with no ultimate support. Now realize that the true foundation is Allah's eternity. In what area of your life today do you need to replace anxiety with trust in that unchanging foundation?

Proof of Allah's Everlastingness (Baqa')
Sanusi proves Allah's everlastingness via logical necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah's existence must be perpetual and how the proof from necessity establishes His everlastingness.

Core Idea
If Allah could cease to exist, He would be contingent, contradicting His necessary existence.

In this passage, Sanusi presents a concise logical proof that Allah is everlasting (bāq). The argument is a reductio: if non-existence were possible, then Allah's existence would be possible rather than necessary, but possible beings are originated, which would clash with His established eternity. Let's unpack this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage once to get the overall argument.
Notice the strong conclusion: 'How could that be?'
2
Identify the conditional statement
Look for the 'if... then' structure: if non-existence were possible, then eternity would be negated.
The condition is 'لَوْ أَمْكَنَ أَنْ يَلْحَقَهُ الْعَدَمُ'.
3
Understand the consequence
See why the possibility of non-existence would reduce Allah's existence to merely possible, which contradicts His necessity.
The key shift is from necessary (wājib) to possible (jā'iz).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْبَقَاءِ لَهُ تَعَالَى : فَلَأَنَّهُ لَوْ أَمْكَنَ أَنْ يَلْحَقَهُ الْعَدَمُ لَانْتَفَىٰ عَنْهُ الْقِدَمُ ; لِكَوْنِ وُجُودِهِ حِينَئِذٍ يَصِيرُ جَائِزًا لَا وَاجِبًا ، وَالْجَائِزُ لَا يَكُونُ وُجُودُهُ إِلَّا حَادِثاً ، كَيْفَ وَقَدْ سَبَقَ قَرِيباً وُجُوبُ قِدَمِهِ تَعَالَى ؟!
And as for the proof of the necessity of everlastingness for Him, exalted: because if it were possible that non-existence could overtake Him, then eternity would be negated from Him, because His existence would then become possible (jā'iz) and not necessary (wājib), and the possible only has existence as originated. How could that be when the necessity of His eternity has just been established?
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This proves that Allah must be everlasting (baqā'). It argues that if His non-existence were possible, then His existence would be merely possible (jāʾiz), not necessary (wājib). But possible things are originated (ḥādith), which would contradict His proven eternity (qidam). Therefore, His existence must be perpetual.

Key Terms
وجوب البقاء
باق
جائز
واجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah could cease to exist.
Correction: The argument shows that if non-existence were possible, Allah would be contingent, contradicting His necessary and eternal nature.

Checkpoint
Why is Allah necessarily everlasting (باق)?
A) Because He said so
B) Because if non-existence were possible, His existence would be possible, contradicting His proven eternity
C) Because He created everything
D) Because He is good

Key Takeaway
Allah's existence is necessarily perpetual because if it were not, He would be contingent, contradicting His proven eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's existence were contingent, what would that mean for your personal certainty in His promises? How does this proof change how you rely on Him?
?
Reflect on a moment when you doubted that Allah will remain faithful to you forever. How does the logical necessity of His everlastingness confront that doubt?
?
This proof shows that Allah cannot cease to exist. Does your devotion reflect a belief in an everlasting Lord, or do you treat Him as though He might not be there tomorrow? What would change if you truly lived this certainty?

Proof of the Necessity of Power, Will, Knowledge, and Life
Sanusi proves that God must have power, will, knowledge, and life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that Allah must possess the attributes of power, will, knowledge, and life, and why the existence of contingent events depends on them.

Core Idea
Contingent events cannot exist without God's power, will, knowledge, and life.

Sanusi now presents a concise logical argument for four essential divine attributes. He shows that the existence of the contingent world itself requires these attributes in the Creator. This proof ties together causality and necessity in a single compelling statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic sentence carefully, then the English translation. Notice the concise structure and the four attributes listed.
The Arabic uses a conditional structure: 'if... then...'.
2
Identify the four attributes and the conditional
List the four attributes: power, will, knowledge, life. Note how the proof is a conditional: if any were absent, no contingent events would exist.
The attributes are essential for creation to occur.
3
Understand the logical necessity
Ask yourself: why does the existence of contingent events prove these attributes? The answer is that each attribute plays a necessary role: power enables, will specifies, knowledge directs, and life is a prerequisite.
This is a standard kalam proof for divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ اتِّصَافِهِ تَعَالَى بِالْقُدْرَةِ وَالْإِرَادَةِ وَالْعِلْمِ وَالْحَيَاةِ : فَلَأَنَّهُ لَوِ انْتَفَى شَيْءٌ مِنْهَا لَمَا وُجِدَ شَيْءٌ مِنَ الْحَوَادِثِ .
As for the proof of the necessity of His being described with power, will, knowledge, and life: it is that if any of them were absent, nothing of the contingent events would exist.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof that God must possess four essential attributes: power (قدرة), will (إرادة), knowledge (علم), and life (حياة). The argument is that if any of these attributes were missing, no contingent events (حوادث) could exist, because power is needed to create, will to specify, knowledge to direct, and life as a condition for these attributes.

Key Terms

إرادة
علم
حياة
حوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God could create the world without having will or knowledge.
Correction: Sanusi argues that contingent events cannot exist without all four attributes; if any were missing, creation would be impossible.

Checkpoint
What would happen if God lacked any of these attributes?
A) The world would still exist
B) Nothing would exist from contingent events
C) God would be weaker
D) Only power would be needed

Key Takeaway
The existence of contingent events necessarily implies that God possesses power, will, knowledge, and life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your every breath depends on God possessing power, will, knowledge, and life in this very moment, would you live today differently? What is one thing you will do before you sleep tonight to acknowledge that dependence?
?
Are there areas of your life where you act as if God's will doesn't matter, or as if His knowledge is incomplete? Identify one such area and write a prayer surrendering it to His complete authority.
?
This proof shows that without any one of these attributes, you would not exist. Reflect on your existence as a constant testimony to these attributes. How will you remind yourself tomorrow of at least one of these attributes each time you see a contingent event (like a breath, a thought, a movement)?

Proofs for Hearing, Sight, and Speech
Sanusi gives transmitted and rational proofs for these attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two proofs (transmitted and rational) that establish the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech as divine attributes.

Core Idea
Two proofs—revelation and reason—together affirm these attributes of Allah.

Sanusi now turns to proving specific attributes: hearing, sight, and speech. He offers two complementary proofs: one from the transmitted sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, consensus) and one from rational necessity. The rational argument is especially important because it shows that these attributes are not merely revealed but rationally required.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully. Notice the structure: first the transmitted proof, then the rational proof introduced by 'وأيضاً'.
2
Understand the transmitted proof
Identify the three sources: Kitab (Qur'an), Sunnah, and Ijma'. This is the transmitted evidence for these attributes.
The footnote (2) clarifies that consensus refers to that of the Companions based on Arabic language.
3
Understand the rational proof
The rational proof uses a logical conditional: if God did not have these attributes, He would have their opposites (deafness, blindness, muteness), which are deficiencies. Since deficiency is impossible for God, He must have these attributes.
4
Reflect on the combination
Notice how Sanusi uses both types of proof together. This shows that kalam relies on revelation and reason harmoniously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ السَّمْعِ لَهُ تَعَالَى وَالْبَصَرِ وَالْكَلَامِ : فَالْكِتَابُ وَالسُّنَّةُ وَالإجْمَاعُ (۲) ، وَأَيْضاً : لَوْ لَمْ يَتَّصِفُ بِهَا لَزِمَ أَنْ يَتَّصِفَ بِأَضْدَادِهَا ، وَهِيَ نَقَائِصُ ، وَالنَّقْصُ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى مُحَالٌ
As for the proof of the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech for Him, Exalted: the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus (2), and also: if He were not described with them, it would necessitate that He be described with their opposites, which are deficiencies, and deficiency is impossible for Him, Exalted.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage provides two proofs for God's attributes of hearing (سمع), sight (بصر), and speech (كلام). The first proof is transmitted: the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus (with the understanding of Arabic language as per footnote 2). The second proof is rational: if God lacked these attributes, He would have their opposites (deafness, blindness, muteness), which are deficiencies, and deficiency is impossible for God.

Key Terms
سمع
بصر
كلام
نقائص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think these attributes are only known through revelation and not rationally provable.
Correction: Sanusi demonstrates that in addition to transmitted evidence, there is a strong rational argument: the absence of these attributes would imply deficiencies, which are impossible for God.

Checkpoint
What is the rational proof for hearing, sight, and speech?
A) They are mentioned in the Quran
B) If God lacked them, He would have deficiencies
C) Everything in the world has them
D) They are necessary for creation

Key Takeaway
Sanusi uses both transmitted and rational proofs to show that hearing, sight, and speech are necessary attributes of Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that Allah possesses hearing, sight, and speech as necessary attributes. But do you truly live as if He hears every word you whisper, sees every secret glance, and speaks to you through His book? What specific change in your daily conduct would reflect that belief more honestly?
?
The rational proof shows that denying these attributes implies deficiency in Allah. Have you ever, in moments of hardship or discontent, subconsciously attributed deficiency to Allah by doubting His wisdom or justice? How can you actively combat that thought today?
?
If deficiency is impossible for Allah, then His hearing and sight are perfect and never fail. How does that truth confront your fear of being abandoned or unheard in your du'a? What will you pray for now, knowing that His hearing is inseparable from His mercy?

Proof that God's Actions are Permissible
Sanusi argues that God's actions are neither obligatory nor impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God's actions regarding contingent things are considered permissible (ja'iz) – neither obligatory (wajib) nor impossible (mustahil).

Core Idea
God's actions on contingent things are permissible, not obligatory or impossible.

Sanusi presents a concise yet powerful proof that God's actions (or refraining from them) concerning contingent beings are permissible. He uses a logical reductio ad absurdum: if such actions were obligatory or impossible, the very nature of contingency would be overturned, which is rationally untenable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Let the author's flow come through before interpreting.
2
Understand the logical argument
Sanusi argues that if an action were obligatory upon God, the contingent would become necessary; if impossible, it would become impossible. Both are absurd because contingency is by definition neither necessary nor impossible.
This is a proof by contradiction.
3
Note the footnote on 'burhan'
The commentary clarifies that 'burhan' (proof) here is used metaphorically because it is not a logical syllogism but a transmitted argument based on understanding language and consensus.
This highlights the methodological nuance in kalam.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
This establishes that God's actions are free and not compelled – they are purely permissible, consistent with His absolute power and will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ كَوْنِ فِعْل الْمُمْكِنَاتِ أَوْ تَرْكِهَا جَائِزاً في حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى : فَلَأَنَّهُ لَوْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى شَيْءٌ مِنْهَا عَفْلاً أَوِ اسْتَحَالَ عَقْلاً .. لانْقَلَبَ الْمُمْكِنُ وَاجِباً أَوْ مُسْتَحِيلاً وَذَلِكَ لا يُعْقَلُ . (۱) إطلاق البرهان هنا على الدليل مجاز ; لعدم تركيبه، ولكونه نقلياً (۲) مع ضميمة فهم أهل اللغة . « دسوقي » ( ص ۱۹۹ ) .
As for the proof that doing or leaving contingent actions is permissible in His right, Exalted: it is that if something of them were obligatory upon Him or rationally impossible... the contingent would become obligatory or impossible, and that is not intelligible. (1) The use of 'burhan' here for 'dalil' is metaphorical; because it is not composed [of premises] and because it is transmitted. (2) With the addition of the understanding of the people of language. 'Desouqi' (p. 199).
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage proves that God's actions regarding contingent things are permissible (جايز), meaning they are neither obligatory nor impossible. If they were obligatory, the contingent would become necessary; if impossible, the contingent would become impossible—both are absurd. The footnote (1) clarifies that the term 'burhan' (proof) is used metaphorically here because this proof is not a logical syllogism but a transmitted argument. Footnote (2) reiterates the need for understanding Arabic language in interpreting consensus.

Key Terms
ممكنات
جائز
واجب
مستحيل
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What would happen if God's actions were obligatory?
A) The contingent would become permissible
B) The contingent would become impossible
C) The contingent would become obligatory
D) Nothing would change

Key Takeaway
God's actions regarding contingent things are permissible, as shown by the absurdity of them being obligatory or impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the proof that God's actions are permissible shatter your hidden assumption that God 'should' act a certain way in your life? Will you release your expectations and trust His freedom even when you don't understand?
?
If God owes you nothing—no obligation to grant your prayers or spare your trials—does that terrify you or free you? How will you adjust your relationship with Him today in light of this truth?
?
When you catch yourself feeling entitled to God's favor, what specific phrase from this proof can you recite to remind yourself that His actions are permissible, not obligatory? Commit to using it the next time you feel entitled.

Attributes Necessitated by Creation's Dependence
Sanusi explains the attributes necessitated by the dependence of all things on Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the dependence of all things on Allah necessitates that He possesses life, universal power, will, and knowledge.

Core Idea
Creation's dependence on Allah proves His life, power, will, and knowledge.

Having established Allah's self-sufficiency, Sanusi now examines the other side of the relationship: the absolute dependence of everything else upon Him. This dependence is not a passive fact; it actively requires that Allah possesses certain attributes without which He could not sustain creation. In this passage, he identifies four such attributes and provides a concise logical proof for each.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four attributes
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. List the four attributes that Sanusi derives from the dependence of creation on Allah.
Notice that the attributes are life, universal power, will, and knowledge.
2
Understand the conditional proof
Sanusi uses a conditional argument: if any of these attributes were missing, Allah would not be able to bring about any created things. Since creation exists and depends on Him, these attributes must be present.
This is a 'conditional necessity' argument common in kalam.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical conclusion
The passage ends with a rhetorical question that reinforces the absurdity of creation depending on a being lacking these attributes. Consider why this style is effective.
Rhetorical questions are often used to emphasize the obviousness of the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا افْتِقَارُ كُلِّ مَا سِوَاهُ إِلَيْهِ : فَهُوَ يُوجِبُ لَهُ تَعَالَى الْحَيَاةَ ، وَعُمُومَ الْقُدْرَةِ ، وَالإِرَادَةِ ، وَالْعِلْم ; إذْ لَوِ انْتَفَى شَيْءٌ مِنْ هَذِهِ لَمَا أَمْكَنَ أَنْ يُوجِدَ تَعَالَى شَيْئاً مِنَ الْحَوَادِثِ ، فَلا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَيْهِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ شَيْءٌ ، كَيْفَ وَهُوَ تَعَالَى الَّذِي يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَيْهِ كُلُّ مَا سِوَاهُ ؟!
As for the dependence (iftiqar) of everything other than Him upon Him: it necessitates for Him Most High: life (al-hayah), and universal power (al-qudrah), and will (al-iradah), and knowledge (al-'ilm); for if any of these were absent, His Most High would not be able to bring into existence any of the originated things, so nothing would be dependent upon Him (Glorified and Exalted), how (could that be) when He Most High is the One upon Whom everything other than Him depends?!
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a proof section. The author now turns to the second component of uluhiyyah: iftiqar (dependence) of all creation upon Allah. He states that this dependence necessitates four attributes: life (hayat), universal power (qudrah), will (iradah), and knowledge ('ilm). The proof is conditional: if any of these attributes were absent, Allah would not be able to create any originated things (hawadith). But since creation does occur and everything depends on Him, these attributes must exist. The argument concludes with a rhetorical question emphasizing that it is impossible for creation to depend on a being lacking these attributes, as that would contradict the very fact of dependence.

Key Terms
افْتِقَار
حَيَاة
قُدْرَة
عُمُوم الْقُدْرَة
إِرَادَة
عِلْم
حَوَادِث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that iftiqar only proves Allah's power, but it also proves life, will, and knowledge as necessary for creation.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly includes life, will, and knowledge as necessary alongside power, because without them, creation could not occur.

Checkpoint
Which attribute is NOT directly derived from the dependence (iftiqar) of all things on Allah?
A) Life
B) Eternity
C) Power
D) Knowledge

Key Takeaway
The dependence of all creation on Allah directly proves that Allah possesses life, all-encompassing power, will, and knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every moment of your existence depends on Allah’s life, power, will, and knowledge, how would your trust in your own plans change? What is one area of your life where you act as if you are independent of Him?
?
The proof shows that without life, Allah could not create. Your own life is a sign of His life. Do you live in a way that acknowledges that your life is a borrowed reflection of His? What would it mean to 'live' as someone wholly dependent on the Living One?
?
Consider the attribute of will. The fact that you exist is because Allah willed it. Are there aspects of your life where you resist His will, as if you have independent power? What would it look like to surrender that area today?

The Six Essential Attributes of God
Sanusi enumerates the essential attributes and argues for the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six essential attributes that are necessary for God and why hearing, sight, and speech are included among them.

Core Idea
God's essential attributes are inseparable from His essence; otherwise He would be in need.

Sanusi begins by enumerating the attributes that are necessarily true of God: existence, eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to contingent beings, self-subsistence, and transcendence from deficiencies. He then expands this list to include hearing, sight, and speech, arguing that if these were not necessary, God would be dependent on something else. This lesson examines that foundational list and its logical grounding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and list the attributes
Carefully read the Arabic passage and identify the six attributes mentioned at the beginning. Then notice that three more are added.
2
Understand the argument for necessity
Sanusi argues that hearing, sight, and speech must be necessary for God; otherwise He would need an originator, a substrate, or someone to repel deficiencies.
This argument links necessity to self-sufficiency.
3
Reflect on self-sufficiency
Why would a contingent attribute imply need? Discuss how necessity removes dependency.
This sets the stage for later implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَعَالَى : الْوُجُودَ ، وَالْقِدَمَ ، وَالْبَقَاءَ ، وَالْمُخَالَفَةَ لِلْحَوَادِثِ ، وَالْقِيَامَ بِالنَّفْسِ ، وَالتَّنَزُهَ عَنِ النَّقَائِصِ وَيَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ : وُجُوبُ السَّمْع لَهُ تَعَالَى ، وَالْبَصَرِ وَالْكَلامِ ؛ إِذْ لَوْ لَمْ تَجِبْ لَهُ تَعَالَى هَذِهِ الصَّفَاتُ لَكَانَ مُحْتَاجاً إِلَى الْمُحْدِثِ أَوِ الْمَحَلِّ أَوْ مَنْ يَدْفَعُ عَنْهُ النَّقَائِصَ وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ : تَنَزَّهُهُ تَعَالَى عَنِ الْأَغْرَاضِ فِي أَفْعَالِهِ وَأَحْكَامِهِ ، وَإِلا لَزِمَ افْتِقَارُهُ تَعَالَى إِلَى مَا يُحَصِّلُ غَرَضَهُ ، كَيْفَ وَهُوَ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الْغَنِيُّ عَنْ كُلِّ مَا سِوَاهُ ؟! وَكَذَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ أَيْضاً : أَنَّهُ لا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى فِعْلُ شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَلا تَرْكُهُ ؛ إذْ لَوْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى شَيْءٌ مِنْهَا عَقْلاً ؛ كَالثَّوَابِ مَثَلاً .. لَكَانَ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ مُفْتَقِراً إِلَى ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء لِيَتَكَمَّلَ بِهِ ؛ إذ لا يَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى إِلا مَا هُوَ كَمَالٌ لَهُ ، كَيْفَ وَهُوَ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الْغَنِيُّ عَنْ كُلَّ مَا سِوَاهُ ؟!
Exalted is He: existence, eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to contingent beings, self-subsistence, and transcendence from deficiencies. And included in that is the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech for Him, Exalted; for if these attributes were not necessary for Him, Exalted, He would be in need of an originator, or a substrate, or someone to repel deficiencies from Him. And from it is taken: His, Exalted, transcendence from purposes in His actions and rulings; otherwise His, Exalted, dependency upon something that fulfills His purpose would follow, and how is He, Majestic and Mighty, the Self-Sufficient from everything other than Him?! And similarly from it is also taken: that no act or omission of any possible thing is obligatory upon Him, Exalted; for if something of them were obligatory upon Him, Exalted, rationally, such as reward, He, Majestic and Mighty, would be in need of that thing to be perfected by it, since nothing is obligatory in His, Exalted, right except that which is perfection for Him; and how is He, Majestic and Mighty, the Self-Sufficient from everything other than Him?!
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of a discussion on divine attributes. It begins by listing attributes that are necessary for God: existence, eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to contingent beings, self-subsistence, and transcendence from deficiencies. Then it expands this list to include the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech, arguing that if these were not necessary, God would be in need of something else—either an originator to bring Him into being, a substrate to inhere in, or someone to remove imperfections—which is impossible. From the same principle of God's self-sufficiency, two further implications are derived. First, God is free from any purposes in His actions and rulings, because having a purpose would imply need for that purpose, contradicting His absolute self-sufficiency. Second, nothing is obligatory upon God from among possible things, such as rewarding the obedient, because obligation would entail that God requires something external to reach perfection, which is incompatible with His being the Self-Sufficient. The argument consistently invokes God's complete independence from everything else as the foundation.

Key Terms
الْوُجُود (existence)
الْقِدَم (eternity)
الْبَقَاء (perpetuity)
الْمُخَالَفَة لِلْحَوَادِث (dissimilarity to contingent beings)
الْقِيَام بِالنَّفْس (self-subsistence)
التَّنَزُه عَنِ النَّقَائِص (transcendence from deficiencies)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The necessity of multiple attributes implies that God is composed of parts.
Correction: These attributes are not separate parts; they are inseparable aspects of God's single essence, and their necessity does not imply composition.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why must hearing, sight, and speech be necessary attributes of God?
A) Because they are mentioned in revelation.
B) Because if they were not necessary, God would be in need of something else.
C) Because God rewards and punishes.
D) Because humans possess these attributes.

Key Takeaway
God possesses a set of essential attributes that are necessary for His being; among them are hearing, sight, and speech, without which He would be in need.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God were in any way in need, He would not be God. In what areas of your life do you still act as if God needs your worship or obedience to be complete? How will you realign your motivation to pure gratitude rather than obligation?
?
God hears and sees everything, and His attributes are inseparable from His essence. Does the reality that you are always before the All-Hearing, All-Seeing shape your private thoughts and actions? What one specific habit would you change today if you truly believed His hearing and sight are necessary and constant?

God's Freedom from Purposes and Obligations
Sanusi derives God's transcendence from purposes and the non-obligation of acts from His self-sufficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God is free from any purposes in His actions and why nothing is obligatory upon Him from among possible things.

Core Idea
God's absolute self-sufficiency entails that He has no purposes and no obligations.

From the same principle that God is self-sufficient, Sanusi derives two important implications: God is not motivated by any external purpose, and He is not obligated to do or refrain from any possible act. This lesson explores these derivations and their theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two implications
Read the passage and find the two conclusions: God's transcendence from purposes, and that nothing is obligatory upon Him.
2
Understand the reasoning for each
For purposes: if God acted for a purpose, He would need that purpose to be fulfilled, contradicting self-sufficiency. For obligation: if an act were obligatory, God would need it for perfection, also contradicting self-sufficiency.
Both rely on the concept of need.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical question
Sanusi twice asks: 'how is He the Self-Sufficient from everything other than Him?' This emphasizes the contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَعَالَى : الْوُجُودَ ، وَالْقِدَمَ ، وَالْبَقَاءَ ، وَالْمُخَالَفَةَ لِلْحَوَادِثِ ، وَالْقِيَامَ بِالنَّفْسِ ، وَالتَّنَزُهَ عَنِ النَّقَائِصِ وَيَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ : وُجُوبُ السَّمْع لَهُ تَعَالَى ، وَالْبَصَرِ وَالْكَلامِ ؛ إِذْ لَوْ لَمْ تَجِبْ لَهُ تَعَالَى هَذِهِ الصَّفَاتُ لَكَانَ مُحْتَاجاً إِلَى الْمُحْدِثِ أَوِ الْمَحَلِّ أَوْ مَنْ يَدْفَعُ عَنْهُ النَّقَائِصَ وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ : تَنَزَّهُهُ تَعَالَى عَنِ الْأَغْرَاضِ فِي أَفْعَالِهِ وَأَحْكَامِهِ ، وَإِلا لَزِمَ افْتِقَارُهُ تَعَالَى إِلَى مَا يُحَصِّلُ غَرَضَهُ ، كَيْفَ وَهُوَ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الْغَنِيُّ عَنْ كُلِّ مَا سِوَاهُ ؟! وَكَذَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ أَيْضاً : أَنَّهُ لا يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى فِعْلُ شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ وَلا تَرْكُهُ ؛ إذْ لَوْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى شَيْءٌ مِنْهَا عَقْلاً ؛ كَالثَّوَابِ مَثَلاً .. لَكَانَ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ مُفْتَقِراً إِلَى ذَلِكَ الشَّيْء لِيَتَكَمَّلَ بِهِ ؛ إذ لا يَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى إِلا مَا هُوَ كَمَالٌ لَهُ ، كَيْفَ وَهُوَ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الْغَنِيُّ عَنْ كُلَّ مَا سِوَاهُ ؟!
Exalted is He: existence, eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to contingent beings, self-subsistence, and transcendence from deficiencies. And included in that is the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech for Him, Exalted; for if these attributes were not necessary for Him, Exalted, He would be in need of an originator, or a substrate, or someone to repel deficiencies from Him. And from it is taken: His, Exalted, transcendence from purposes in His actions and rulings; otherwise His, Exalted, dependency upon something that fulfills His purpose would follow, and how is He, Majestic and Mighty, the Self-Sufficient from everything other than Him?! And similarly from it is also taken: that no act or omission of any possible thing is obligatory upon Him, Exalted; for if something of them were obligatory upon Him, Exalted, rationally, such as reward, He, Majestic and Mighty, would be in need of that thing to be perfected by it, since nothing is obligatory in His, Exalted, right except that which is perfection for Him; and how is He, Majestic and Mighty, the Self-Sufficient from everything other than Him?!
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of a discussion on divine attributes. It begins by listing attributes that are necessary for God: existence, eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to contingent beings, self-subsistence, and transcendence from deficiencies. Then it expands this list to include the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech, arguing that if these were not necessary, God would be in need of something else—either an originator to bring Him into being, a substrate to inhere in, or someone to remove imperfections—which is impossible. From the same principle of God's self-sufficiency, two further implications are derived. First, God is free from any purposes in His actions and rulings, because having a purpose would imply need for that purpose, contradicting His absolute self-sufficiency. Second, nothing is obligatory upon God from among possible things, such as rewarding the obedient, because obligation would entail that God requires something external to reach perfection, which is incompatible with His being the Self-Sufficient. The argument consistently invokes God's complete independence from everything else as the foundation.

Key Terms
الْغَنِي (the Self-Sufficient)
الْأَغْرَاض (purposes)
الْكَمَال (perfection)
الْوُجُوب (obligation)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would follow if God had a purpose for His actions?
A) His actions would be wise.
B) He would be dependent on that purpose.
C) He would be more perfect.
D) He would be just.

Key Takeaway
God is completely self-sufficient; thus He has no need for purposes or for anything to perfect Him, so nothing can be obligatory upon Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God has no need for your worship and no obligation to reward you, what truly motivates you to pray, fast, and obey? Is your worship for Him alone, or are you seeking something for yourself? How can you purify your intention today?
?
The passage teaches that God does nothing for a purpose outside Himself. This means that the trials you face may not have a purpose you can understand. Can you trust God even when His actions seem purposeless to you? What would it take for you to surrender that need for explanation?
?
You likely believe that good deeds should be rewarded and evil punished. But this lesson says nothing is obligatory upon God. How does that challenge your sense of fairness? Will you still obey God even if you cannot demand justice from Him? Examine your heart: are you serving God or your own sense of entitlement?
