The Permissibility of Applying the Term 'Al-Qadim' to Allah
Sanusi discusses the disagreement on whether to apply the term 'al-Qadim' to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement on whether to utter the term 'al-Qadim' for Allah and the evidence that resolves it.

Core Idea
The term 'al-Qadim' is proven by the Sunnah and consensus, despite not being in the Quran.

Sanusi presents a debate among scholars: can we call Allah 'al-Qadim' (the Eternal)? Some hesitate because it is not in the Quran. But he shows that the Sunnah and consensus support its use. Let's examine the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two opinions and the evidence cited.
2
Identify the two positions
Find the view that permits 'al-Qadim' because its meaning is proven, and the view that avoids it on the basis of tawqifiyya.
3
Examine the evidence
Look at the references: al-Halimi's inclusion in the 99 names, the hadith from Ibn Majah, and the consensus cited by al-Sa'd.
4
Understand the resolution
See how the author concludes that the term is permissible based on these proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلاف في جواز إطلاق لفظ (القديم) عليه سبحانه وهل يجوز أن يُتلفظ بلفظ (القديم) في حقه تعالى فيقال هو جل وعز قديم لأن معناه واجب له جل وعز عقلاً ونقلاً أو لا يُتلفظ بذلك وإنما يقال يجب له تعالى القدم أو نحو هذا من العبارات ولا يطلق عليه في اللفظ اسم (القديم) لأن أسماءه جل وعز توقيفية هذا مما تردد فيه بعض المشايخ لكن قال العراقي في «شرح أصول السبكي» : عدة الحليمي في الأسماء وقال لم يرد في الكتاب نصا ولكن ورد في السنة قال العراقي وأشار بذلك إلى ما رواه ابن ماجه في «سننه» من حديث أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه وفيه عد (القديم) من التسعة والتسعين واستدل العلامة السعد في «شرح العقائد» بالإجماع
The disagreement on the permissibility of uttering the term 'al-Qadim' regarding Him, Exalted is He. Is it permissible to utter the term 'al-Qadim' with respect to Him, Exalted, so that we say: He, Mighty and Majestic, is Qadim, because its meaning is obligatory for Him, Mighty and Majestic, by reason and transmission? Or is it not to be uttered, but rather it is said: 'al-Qidam is obligatory for Him, Exalted,' or something like this phrasing, and the name 'al-Qadim' is not applied to Him verbally because His names, Mighty and Majestic, are tawqifiyya (derived from revelation)? This is something about which some of the mashayikh hesitated. However, al-'Iraqi said in his 'Sharh Usul al-Subki': 'Al-Halimi counted it among the names, and said: It did not occur in the Book as a text, but it did occur in the Sunnah.' Al-'Iraqi said: 'And he indicated by that to what Ibn Majah narrated in his Sunan from the hadith of Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, in which is the counting of "al-Qadim" among the ninety-nine.' And al-Sa'd in his 'Sharh al-'Aqa'id' adduced consensus.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage presents a difference of opinion among scholars about uttering the term 'al-Qadim' (the Eternal) in reference to Allah. The first view permits it because its meaning—that Allah has no beginning—is established by reason and revelation. The second view avoids the term because Allah's names are tawqifiyya (derived only from revelation), and 'al-Qadim' is not explicitly in the Quran. The author notes that some scholars hesitated, but then he cites al-'Iraqi, who reports that al-Halimi included 'al-Qadim' among the ninety-nine names, relying on a hadith from Ibn Majah. Finally, al-Sa'd is mentioned as adducing consensus (ijma') as further evidence. The passage thus resolves the disagreement by showing that the term is supported by the Sunnah and consensus.

Key Terms
القديم (al-Qadim)
القدم (al-Qidam)
توقيفية (tawqifiyya)
الأسماء (al-Asma')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'al-Qadim' cannot be used for Allah because it is not in the Quran.
Correction: The passage shows it is found in the Sunnah and supported by consensus, so it is permissible.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what evidence did al-'Iraqi provide for the permissibility of using the term 'al-Qadim'?
A) Quranic verse
B) Sunnah via Ibn Majah's hadith
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Rational proof

Key Takeaway
Although 'al-Qadim' is not explicitly in the Quran, it is established as a name of Allah through the Sunnah and consensus of scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that a name for Allah is not in the Quran, do you immediately reject it, or do you trust the scholars who find evidence from the Sunnah and consensus? What does your reaction reveal about your submission to the full scope of revelation?
?
This lesson shows that even respected scholars hesitated on this issue. Is there an area of your faith where you are hesitating due to caution? What evidence from the Sunnah or consensus could move you from hesitation to conviction?
?
If someone challenged you, saying 'al-Qadim' is an innovation because it's not in the Quran, would you be able to defend the name based on what you learned? Are you willing to stand on the authority of the Prophet's Sunnah and scholarly consensus, even when it feels less direct?

Defining al-Baqa' and Refuting the Nafsi View
Sanusi defines al-baqa' and refutes the nafsi view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-baqa' as the negation of subsequent non-existence, the alternative view that it is a nafsi attribute, and the reason why that view is considered weak.

Core Idea
Al-baqa' is not an essential attribute; it is the negation of non-existence after existence.

Sanusi begins by defining the divine attribute of al-baqa' (permanence). He presents the standard definition and then an alternative interpretation that would make both al-baqa' and al-qidam essential attributes. He then argues against this view, explaining why it is weak. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the opening definition of al-baqa' as the negation of subsequent non-existence.
Notice the precise wording: 'salb al-'adam al-lahiq lil-wujud'.
2
Consider the alternative view
Notice the alternative definition offered by some imams and how it equates al-baqa' with existence continued in the future.
This leads to considering both qidam and baqa' as nafsi attributes.
3
Analyze the refutation
Identify the author's proof that al-baqa' cannot be a nafsi attribute because the essence can be conceived without it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْبَقَاءُ صفة البقاء هو عبارة عن سلب العدم اللاحق للوجود وبعض الأئمة يقولُ : معنى (البقاء) في حقِّهِ تعالى : استمرار الوجودِ في المستقبل إلى غير نهايةٍ ، كما أنَّ القدم في حقِّهِ تعالى : استمرار الوجودِ في الماضي إلى غيرِ غاية وكأنَّ هذه العبارةَ يجنح قائلُها إلى أنَّ القدم والبقاء صفتان نفسيتانِ ؛ لأنَّهما عندَه الوجود المستمرُّ في الماضي والمستقبل ، والوجود نفسي ؛ لعدم تحقق الذاتِ بدونه ، وهذا المذهب ضعيفٌ ؛ لأنَّهما لو كانا نفسيَّين لزمَ أَلا تُعقَلَ الذات بدونهما ، وذلك باطل ؛ بدليل أنَّ الذات يُعقَلُ وجودها ، ثم
And al-Baqa' is the attribute of permanence. It is an expression meaning the negation of subsequent non-existence to existence. And some imams say: The meaning of al-Baqa' with respect to Him, Exalted, is the continuation of existence in the future without end, just as al-Qidam with respect to Him, Exalted, is the continuation of existence in the past without limit. It is as if the proponent of this expression inclines to the view that al-Qidam and al-Baqa' are nafsiyya (essential) attributes, because according to him they are existence continued in the past and future, and existence is nafsi, since the essence is not realized without it. And this madhhab is weak, because if they were nafsiyya, it would entail that the essence cannot be conceived without them, and that is false, as evidenced by the fact that the essence is conceived as existing, then...
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of al-baqa' (permanence/future-eternity) and then refutes an alternative understanding. The author gives the standard definition: al-baqa' is the negation of subsequent non-existence for an existent. Then he presents the view of some imams who define it as the continuation of existence in the future without end, analogous to al-qidam being continuation in the past. The author notes that this alternative definition leads its proponents to consider both al-qidam and al-baqa' as nafsi (essential) attributes, because they equate them with existence itself, which is nafsi. The author then declares this madhhab weak, providing a proof: if they were nafsi, the essence (dhat) could not be conceived without them; however, we can conceive the essence as existent without yet considering its past or future continuation. The proof is cut off at the page break but the key point is present.

Key Terms
البقاء (al-Baqa')
القدم (al-Qidam)
صفة نفسية (nafsi attribute)
الوجود (al-wujud)
الذات (al-dhat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-baqa' and al-qidam are essential (nafsi) attributes that cannot be separated from the essence.
Correction: The passage argues that they are not nafsi because the essence can be conceived as existing without considering its past or future continuation.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the view that al-baqa' is a nafsi attribute weak?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran
B) Because the essence can be conceived without it
C) Because it implies multiplicity of eternals
D) Because it is not mentioned in the Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Al-baqa' is defined as the negation of subsequent non-existence for an existent; it is not an essential attribute because the essence can be conceived without reference to its permanence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's permanence is not an essential part of His essence but merely the negation of His ceasing to exist, how does that reshape your gratitude for the fact that you continue to exist each moment? Do you truly rely on Him for your own permanence, or do you live as if your existence is self-guaranteed? Will you pause today to thank Him for sustaining you each second?
?
Sanusi argues that the essence of Allah can be conceived without considering His permanence. This means our minds cannot fully contain Him. When you try to 'grasp' Allah, do you feel frustration or humility? Will you accept the limits of your intellect and worship Him as He is, not as you imagine Him to be?
?
The alternative definition of al-baqa' leads some to make it an essential attribute. Could there be a subtle pride in your heart that makes you want to define Allah too tightly, reducing Him to categories you control? What is one assumption about Allah's attributes you hold that might not be based on the precise teachings of the Salaf? Will you commit to correcting it this week?

The Correct Position on Baqa' and Qidam: Negative Attributes
Sanusi defines baqa', critiques alternative views, and establishes the correct view that both qidam and baqa' are negative attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the verifying scholars consider baqa' and qidam as negative attributes, and how other positions lead to logical problems like infinite regress.

Core Idea
Baqa' and qidam are negations, not independent realities.

Sanusi tackles two important divine attributes: qidam (eternity past) and baqa' (eternity future). Are they real, existing attributes like knowledge and power? No—the verifying scholars affirm they are merely negations. In this lesson, you will follow Sanusi's refutation of mistaken views and his conclusion that both are negative attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation together. Notice the flow of argument: definition, alternative views, refutations, final position.
2
Identify the three incorrect views
Sanusi presents three incorrect positions about qidam and baqa'. Identify each one and the argument against it.
3
Understand the proof for the correct view
Sanusi states that the truth is both are negative. Understand what 'negative attribute' means and why it avoids the problems of other views.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: Why does it matter whether these attributes are positive or negative? How does this relate to the simplicity of God and avoiding infinite regress?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْبَقَاءُ صفة البقاء هو عبارة عن سلب العدم اللاحق للوجود وبعضُ الأئمةِ يقولُ : معنى ( البقاء ) في حقِّهِ تعالى : استمرار الوجودِ في المستقبل إلى غير نهايةٍ ، كما أنَّ القدم في حقِّهِ تعالى : استمرار الوجودِ في الماضي إلى غيرِ غاية(٢) ، وكأنَّ هذه العبارةَ يجنح قائلُها إلى أنَّ القدم والبقاء صفتان نفسيتانِ ؛ لأنَّهما عندَه الوجود المستمرُّ في الماضي والمستقبل ، والوجود نفسي ؛ لعدم تحقق الذاتِ بدونه ، وهذا المذهب ضعيفٌ ؛ لأنَّهما لو كانا نفسيَّين لزمَ أَلا تُعقَلَ الذات بدونهما ، وذلك باطل ؛ بدليل أنَّ الذات يُعقَلُ وجودها ، ثم يُطلب البرهان على وجوب قدمها وبقائها وشَدَّ قومٌ فقالوا (١) : إِنَّ القدمَ والبقاء صفتان موجودتان يقومان بالذات كالعلم والقدرة ، ولا يخفى ضعفُهُ ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ أنْ يكونَ القدم والبقاء قديمينِ أيضاً بقدم آخر موجود ، وباقيين ببقاء آخر موجود ، ثم ننقلُ الكلامَ إلى هذا القدم الآخر وهذا البقاء الآخر فيلزم فيهما ما لزمَ في الأَوَّلَينِ ، ويلزم التسلسل وأضعفُ مِنْ هذا : مَنْ فَرَقَ وقال : القدمُ سلبي ، والبقاء وجودي (٢) والحق الذي عليهِ المحققون : أنَّهما صفتانِ سلبيتانِ ؛ أي : كلُّ واحد منهما عبارةٌ عن نفي معنى لا يليقُ بهِ تعالى ، وليس لهما معنى موجود في الخارج عن الذهنِ
And al-baqa' (eternity future) is the description of baqa': it is an expression for the negation of the subsequent non-existence to existence. And some of the imams say: the meaning of baqa' with respect to Him, exalted is He, is the continuation of existence in the future without end, just as qidam (eternity past) with respect to Him, exalted is He, is the continuation of existence in the past without end. And it is as if the proponent of this expression inclines to the view that qidam and baqa' are essential attributes (nafsiyyān), because in his view they are the continuous existence in the past and future, and existence is essential (nafsī) because the self is not realized without it. This school is weak because if they were essential, the self would not be conceivable without them, and that is false, as evidenced by the fact that the self's existence is conceivable, and then proof is sought for the necessity of its qidam and baqa'. And a group went further and said: indeed qidam and baqa' are existing attributes that subsist in the self, like knowledge and power. Its weakness is not hidden because it would necessitate that qidam and baqa' would also be eternal by another eternal existent, and perpetually enduring by another perpetual endurance; then we transfer the discussion to this other qidam and this other baqa', and what was necessary in the first two is necessary for them, and an infinite regress (tasalsul) would follow. And weaker than this is the one who made a distinction and said: qidam is negative (salbī) and baqa' is positive (wujūdī). And the truth upon which the verifying scholars (muhaqqiqūn) are agreed is that both are negative attributes (sifāt salbiyya), i.e., each of them is an expression for the negation of a meaning that is not befitting Him, exalted is He, and they have no meaning existing externally from the mind.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the attributes baqa' (eternity future) and qidam (eternity past). Sanusi begins by defining baqa' as the negation of subsequent non-existence to existence. He then presents the view of some imams who define baqa' as the continuation of existence in the future without end, similar to qidam as continuation in the past. This view, Sanusi explains, leads to considering both qidam and baqa' as essential attributes (nafsiyyat) because they are identical to existence itself. Sanusi refutes this by pointing out that if they were essential, the self (dhāt) would not be conceivable without them, but the self's existence is conceivable independently; the proof for their necessity is separate. Next, Sanusi presents a stronger view: some hold that qidam and baqa' are real, existing attributes that subsist in the self, like knowledge and power. This leads to infinite regress because each would require another qidam/baqa', and so on. Then a weaker view distinguishes between qidam as negative and baqa' as positive. Finally, Sanusi states the correct position of the verifying scholars (muhaqqiqūn): both are negative attributes (sifāt salbiyya); they are negations of unsuitable meanings and do not have external existence.

القدم
صفة سلبية
صفة نفسية
صفة وجودية
التسلسل
الذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal attributes like qidam and baqa' are positive attributes with external existence.
Correction: They are merely negations of non-existence; they have no independent reality outside the mind.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the correct view regarding the attributes of qidam (eternity past) and baqa' (eternity future)?
A) Both are positive attributes existing externally.
B) Both are negative attributes that negate something unsuitable.
C) Qidam is negative and baqa' is positive.
D) Both are essential attributes identical to existence.

Key Takeaway
Qidam and baqa' are not independent attributes; they are simply the negation of non-existence before and after, respectively.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of God's eternity (baqa'), do you instinctively treat it as a positive quality or as a mere negation of annihilation? How might this subtle shift in understanding deepen your tawhid?
?
Sanusi shows that if qidam and baqa' were essential, God's essence would depend on them. Have you ever held a concept of God that makes His attributes so central that you lose sight of His unqualified existence? Confess that tendency and resolve to purify your 'aqeedah today.
?
The infinite regress argument warns against adding any eternal entity to God. In your heart, do you ever attribute 'eternal' to anything besides Allah, even indirectly? Commit to recognizing that only Allah is eternal by negation of non-existence.

The Proof that Qidam and Baqa' Are Negative Attributes
Sanusi refutes two incorrect views on qidam and baqa' and establishes they are negative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why qidam and baqa' must be negative attributes and how the argument against the two wrong views is constructed.

Core Idea
Qidam and baqa' are negations, not positive entities.

In this passage, Sanusi tackles an important theological question: are God's attributes of eternality and permanence positive or negative? He walks through two mistaken positions and shows why they fail, ultimately affirming that both are purely negative attributes. This distinction is crucial for avoiding infinite regress in divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English translation carefully. Notice the structure: proof requirement, first wrong view, second wrong view, correct view.
Pay attention to the refutation arguments.
2
Identify the two wrong views
Find the two opinions that Sanusi rejects. The first claims both are positive; the second claims one is negative and the other positive. Understand why each is problematic.
The first leads to infinite regress.
3
Grasp the correct position
Understand what it means for both to be negative attributes. Each is simply a negation of an unfitting quality (e.g., not having a beginning, not having an end). They are not separate existent entities.
This is the view of the verifiers (muhaqqiqun).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُطلب البرهان على وجوب قدمها وبقائها
وشدَّ قومٌ فقالوا (١): إِنَّ القدمَ والبقاء صفتان موجودتان يقومان بالذات كالعلم والقدرة، ولا يخفى ضعفُهُ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ أنْ يكونَ القدم والبقاء قديمينِ أيضاً بقدم آخر موجود، وباقيين ببقاء آخر موجود، ثم ننقلُ الكلامَ إلى هذا القدم الآخر وهذا البقاء الآخر فيلزم فيهما ما لزمَ في الأَوَّلَينِ، ويلزم التسلسل
وأضعفُ مِنْ هذا: مَنْ فَرَقَ وقال: القدمُ سلبي، والبقاء وجودي (٢)
والحق الذي عليهِ المحققون: أنَّهما صفتانِ سلبيتانِ؛ أي: كلُّ واحد منهما عبارةٌ عن نفي معنى لا يليقُ بهِ تعالى، وليس لهما معنى موجود في الخارج عن الذهن
The proof is sought for the necessity of His eternality and permanence. And some people insisted and said (1): Indeed, eternality and permanence are two existing attributes that subsist in the Essence like knowledge and power, and its weakness is not hidden; because it necessarily follows that eternality and permanence would also be eternal by another existing eternality, and permanent by another existing permanence. Then we transfer the discussion to this other eternality and this other permanence, and what applied to the first two applies to them, and an infinite regress follows. And weaker than this is the one who differentiated and said: Eternality is negative, and permanence is positive (2). And the truth upon which the verifiers are agreed is that both are negative attributes; that is, each of them is an expression of negating a meaning that is not befitting to Him, may He be exalted, and they have no meaning existing externally to the mind.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation regarding the attributes of qidam (eternity without beginning) and baqa' (permanence without end) for God. The author begins by stating that a proof is required for the necessity of these attributes. Then he presents the first wrong opinion: some claimed that qidam and baqa' are positive attributes that subsist in the Essence like knowledge and power. He refutes this by showing that if they were positive, they would themselves require another eternality and permanence, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul). Next, he presents an even weaker opinion that tries to differentiate by saying qidam is negative but baqa' is positive. He dismisses this without detailed refutation, implying inconsistency. Finally, he states the correct position held by the verifiers (muhaqqiqun): both are negative attributes. That means each is simply the negation of an unfitting meaning (e.g., qidam negates temporal origination, baqa' negates annihilation), and they have no extramental existence as separate entities.

صفة وجودية
التسلسل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qidam and baqa' are positive attributes that exist as entities in God's essence.
Correction: If they were positive, they would themselves need eternality and permanence, causing infinite regress. They are mere negations.

Checkpoint

Qidam and Baqa' Relate to Every Existent
Sanusi states the universal scope of qidam and baqa'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the divine attributes of qidam and baqa' are not exclusive to God but relate to all existents.

Core Idea
Qidam and baqa' encompass all existence.

This passage clarifies the scope of two essential divine attributes: pre-eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa'). Many might assume these are exclusive to God, but Sanusi explicitly states they relate to every existent. Understanding this helps us grasp how divine attributes engage with creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the repetition of 'متعلقتان بكل موجود' which may be a scribal duplication.
The repetition emphasizes the universal scope.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that qidam and baqa' are related to every existent. Ask yourself: what is the significance of this universal relation?
3
Examine the categories
The passage lists three binary categories that cover all existents: old/new, essence/attribute, manifest/hidden. These show that no existent is excluded.
These categories are comprehensive.
4
Reflect on the importance
This shows that the divine attributes are not isolated; they have a relationship with all of creation. It prepares the student for understanding how attributes like knowledge and power also relate to creation.
This connects to the broader kalam framework.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واجبتا القدم والبقاء ، متعلقتان بكل موجود متعلقتان بكل موجود (۱) ؛ قديماً كان أو حادثاً ، ذاتاً كانَ أو صفةً ، ظاهراً كانَ أو باطناً .
The two necessary (attributes) of pre-eternity (qidam) and permanence (baqa') are related to every existent, to every existent (1); whether it is old or new, whether essence or attribute, whether manifest or hidden.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a statement about the scope of the two necessary attributes of God: qidam (pre-eternity) and baqa' (permanence). The author asserts that these two attributes are related (متعلقتان) to every existent (بكل موجود), whether that existent is old or new, essence or attribute, manifest or hidden. This is a key point in kalam because it emphasizes that the divine attributes are not limited to God but have a universal relation to all things. In other words, God's qidam and baqa' encompass all of creation in terms of their ontological relation. The repetition 'متعلقتان بكل موجود' is likely a scribal duplication.

Key Takeaway
The divine attributes of pre-eternity and permanence are not exclusive to God but relate to all existents.

The Meaning of Qiyam bi al-Nafs (Self-Subsistence)
Definition and refutation of misconceptions about divine self-subsistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of qiyam bi al-nafs as God's independence from a locus and a particularizer, and why it refutes misconceptions that God is an attribute.

Core Idea
God's self-subsistence means He needs no place and no creator.

This passage from Sanusi's al-Sanusiyya defines one of the essential divine attributes: qiyam bi al-nafs. It explains that God does not depend on a locus (like an attribute depends on a substance) nor on a particularizer that brings Him into existence. The author also refutes those who wrongly consider God to be an attribute, like the Christians and Batiniyya. Let's examine the text closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the concise style and the two key negations.
The passage includes footnoted clarifications that are part of the learned commentary.
2
Identify the two negations
The definition centers on two things: not needing a locus (maḥall) and not needing a particularizer (mukhaṣṣiṣ). Find these in the Arabic and understand what each means.
3
Understand the refutation
See how the author uses the negation of a locus to reject the Christian and Batiniyya belief that God is an attribute (accident). Understand that God is an essence qualified by attributes, not an attribute itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفة القيام بالنفس وَقِيَامُهُ تَعَالَى بِنَفْسِهِ ؛ أَي : لا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى مَحَلَّ ، وَلا مُخَصِّص . يعني : أَنَّهُ ممَّا يجبُ لهُ تعالى : أنْ يقوم بنفسِهِ (۱) ؛ أي : بذاتِهِ و معنى قيامِهِ تعالى بنفسِهِ : سلبُ افتقارِهِ لشيءٍ مِنَ الأَشياء . فلا يفتقر تعالى إلى محل ؛ أي : ذات سوى ذاتِهِ يوجد فيها كما توجد الصفةُ في الموصوفِ ؛ لأنَّ ذلكَ لا يكون إلا للصفاتِ ، وهو تعالى ذات موصوفٌ بالصفاتِ ، وليس جلَّ وعزَّ بصفة كما تدعيه النصارى ومَنْ في معناهم مِنَ الباطنيَّةِ ، أهلك الله تعالى جميعهم ، وسيأتي برهان ذلكَ إِنْ شاءَ اللهُ تعالى عند تعرُّضنا للبراهين (٢) وكذلك لا يفتقر تعالى إلى مخصص ؛ أي : فاعل يخصصه بالوجودِ ؛ لا في ذاتِهِ ، ولا في صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ ؛ لوجوبِ القدم (١) الظاهر أن الباء للآلة ؛ لأن معنى ) قام بنفسه ( استغنى بنفسه ؛ أي : غَناؤه بنفسه ، لا بالغير ولا بالاكتساب ، فهو إذا أمر حصل له من قبل نفسه سكتاني » ( ق ٣٤ ) ، ويجوز أن تكون الباء سببية ، وظرفية مجازية . (٢) سيأتي ( ص ٢١٥ ) ، والمراد بالنصارى : بعضهم
The attribute of self-subsistence (qiyam bi al-nafs). And His standing by Himself means: He does not need a locus (maḥall), nor a particularizer (mukhaṣṣiṣ). It means that it is of the things necessary for Him, may He be exalted: that He stands by Himself (1); i.e., by His essence. And the meaning of His standing by Himself is: the negation of His need for any of the things. So He, may He be exalted, does not need a locus; i.e., an essence other than His essence in which He exists, as the attribute exists in the described; because that is only for attributes, and He is an essence qualified by attributes, and He is not an attribute as the Christians and those like them from the Bāṭiniyya claim – may Allah destroy all of them – and the proof of that will come, if Allah wills, when we discuss the proofs (2). And likewise, He does not need a particularizer; i.e., an agent that particularizes Him with existence; neither in His essence nor in any of His attributes, because of the necessity of pre-eternity (qidam). (1) Evidently, the ‘ba’’ is for the instrument (ālāt); because the meaning of ‘qāma bi-nafsihi’ is: He is independent by Himself; i.e., His self-sufficiency by Himself, not by another nor by acquisition; so it is a thing that occurs from before Himself ‘saktānī’ (q 34), and it is permissible that the ‘ba’’ be causal (sababiyya) and metaphorical circumstantial (ẓarfiyya majāziyya). (2) It will come (p. 215), and the intended by ‘Christians’ is some of them.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the divine attribute of qiyam bi al-nafs (self-subsistence). The author begins by stating the definition: God's 'standing by Himself' means He does not need a locus (محل) nor a particularizer (مخصص). He then explains that it is necessary for God to be self-subsistent, and the meaning is the negation of His need for anything. Specifically, He does not need a locus, i.e., a separate essence in which He exists, because that would be characteristic of accidents (صفات) which inhere in substances; God is not an accident as the Christians and Bāṭiniyya claim. Rather, He is an essence (ذات) qualified by attributes. The author also states that God does not need a particularizer, i.e., an agent that brings Him into existence, because of the necessity of His pre-eternity (قدم). The passage includes editorial footnotes: one clarifying the grammatical sense of the 'ba'' in 'bi-nafsihi' (instrumental, causal, or metaphorical circumstantial), and another noting that the proof against the Christians will come later and that 'Christians' refers to some of them.

Key Terms
القيام بالنفس
محل
مخصص
ذات
صفة
القدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that God is an attribute (like the Christians and Bāṭiniyya).
Correction: The passage clarifies that God is a self-subsistent essence, not an attribute; attributes inhere in a subject, but God is the subject of attributes.

Checkpoint
What does 'qiyam bi al-nafs' mean for God according to this passage?
A) He is self-sufficient and independent of all things.
B) He does not need a locus or a particularizer.
C) He is an accident that inheres in a substance.
D) He exists within creation.

Key Takeaway
Qiyam bi al-nafs means that Allah is self-sufficient and does not require a locus or a creator, distinguishing Him from all contingent beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if Allah is self-sufficient and you are utterly dependent on Him, or do you in practice rely on created things? This lesson forces you to examine: In what areas of your life are you living as if something else is your support?
?
The passage refutes the idea that Allah is an attribute. Have you ever, in your thoughts, reduced Allah to a concept or a feeling, rather than recognizing Him as the Self-Subsistent Essence? What specific thoughts or habits of mind need to be repented from?
?
If Allah needs no locus and no particularizer, then He is absolutely independent. How should this affect your trust in Him? What would change in your life today if you fully internalized that Allah is not in need of anyone or anything?

The Attribute of Self-Subsistence (al-Qiyam bi al-Nafs)
Sanusi defines self-subsistence and refutes those who deny it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of God's self-subsistence as independence from both a substrate and a specifier, and how this distinguishes Him from all created beings.

Core Idea
Self-subsistence means God depends on nothing—no place, no cause, no agent.

Sanusi now turns to a fundamental attribute: self-subsistence. This attribute affirms that God exists by His own essence without needing a location or an originating cause. It is a cornerstone of Islamic theology, establishing God's absolute independence and refuting those who reduce Him to an attribute or a contingent being. This lesson unpacks the two key negations that define self-subsistence and shows how the Quran confirms it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage together with its literal translation. Notice the technical terms used and the overall structure.
Pay attention to the two negations: no substrate (mahall) and no specifier (mukhassis).
2
Understand the two negations
Identify what 'no substrate' means (God is not an attribute inhering in another essence) and what 'no specifier' means (God was not brought into existence by an agent). The commentary will elaborate.
3
Analyze the refutation
Sanusi refutes the claims of Christians and Batinis who liken God to an attribute. Note the logical reasoning and the promise of a later proof.
The refutation is based on the necessity of pre-eternity for God's essence and attributes.
4
Examine the Quranic support
Read the verses from Surah Fatir and Surah al-Ikhlas. Notice how the term 'al-Samad' implies all creation depends on God.
The phrase 'by the tongue of its state' refers to the inherent need of all things for God.
5
Clarify key distinctions
Sanusi distinguishes between self-subsistence of God and other entities that are independent of a substrate yet still depend on a specifier (like bodies). This highlights the uniqueness of God's independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفة القيام بالنفس. وَقِيَامُهُ تَعَالَى بِنَفْسِهِ ؛ أَي : لا يَفْتَقِرُ إِلَى مَحَلَّ ، وَلا مُخَصِّص. يعني : أَنَّهُ ممَّا يجبُ لهُ تعالى : أنْ يقوم بنفسِهِ (۱) ؛ أي : بذاتِهِ و معنى قيامِهِ تعالى بنفسِهِ : سَلْبُ افتقارِهِ لشيءٍ مِنَ الأَشياء . فلا يفتقر تعالى إلى محل ؛ أي : ذات سوى ذاتِهِ يوجد فيها كما توجد الصفةُ في الموصوفِ ؛ لأنَّ ذلكَ لا يكون إلا للصفاتِ ، وهو تعالى ذات موصوفٌ بالصفاتِ ، وليس جلَّ وعزَّ بصفة كما تدعيه النصارى ومَنْ في معناهم مِنَ الباطنيَّةِ ، أهلك الله تعالى جميعهم ، وسيأتي برهان ذلكَ إِنْ شاءَ اللهُ تعالى عند تعرُّضنا للبراهين (۲). وكذلك لا يفتقر تعالى إلى مخصص ؛ أي : فاعل يخصصه بالوجودِ ؛ لا في ذاتِهِ ، ولا في صفةٍ مِنْ صفاتِهِ ؛ لوجوبِ القدمِ والبَقاءِ لذاتِهِ تعالى ولجميع صفاتِهِ ، وإنَّما يحتاج إلى المخصص - أي : الفاعل - مَنْ يقبلُ العدمَ ، ومولانا جل وعزَّ لا يقبلُه ، فإذا يستحيل على مولانا جل وعزَّ الافتقار عموماً. وبهذا تعرفُ : أنَّ مرادَنا بالمحل في العقيدة الذاتُ ، ومرادَنا بالمخصص الفاعلُ ؛ فبعدم افتقاره تعالى إلى محل - أي : ذاتِ أخرى - لزمَ أَنَّهُ جلَّ وعزَّ ذات لا صفةٌ ، و بعدم افتقاره تعالى إلى مخصص - أي : فاعل - لزمَ أَنَّ ذاتَهُ العليَّةَ جَلَّ وعزَّ ليسَتْ كسائر الذوات التي لا تفتقرُ هي أيضاً إلى محل ؛ كالأجرام مثلاً ؛ لأنَّ هذهِ وإنْ كانَتْ مستغنيةً عن المحل - أي : عن ذات تقوم بها - فهي مفتقرة ابتداءً ودواماً افتقاراً ضرورياً لازماً إلى المخصص ؛ أي : الفاعل ؛ وهو مولانا جل وعزَّ . فإذا ؛ القيام بالنفس : هو عبارةٌ عن الغنى المطلق ، وذلكَ لا يمكنُ أنْ يكونَ إلا لمولانا تبارك وتعالى ، قالَ جلَّ مِنْ قائل : يَأَيُّهَا النَّاسُ أَنتُمُ الْفُقَرَاء إِلَى اللَّهِ وَاللهُ هُوَ الْغَيُّ الْحَمِيدُ [فاطر : ١٥] . وقال تعالى : اللهُ الصَّمَدُ * لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ * وَلَمْ يَكُن لَهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ [الإخلاص : ٢-٤] ، فأثبت تعالى بقوله : والله الصَّمَدُ الافتقار كلِّ ما سواه إليهِ جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ إذ الصمد هو الذي يُصمَدُ إليه في الحوائج ؛ أي: يُقصد فيه ، ومنه تُسألُ ، ولا شكَّ أَنَّ كلَّ ما سواه تعالى صامدٌ إِليه ؛ أي : مفتقر إليه ابتداءً ودواماً ؛ بلسان حالِهِ ، أو بلسان مقاله ، أو بهما معاً.
The attribute of self-subsistence. And His self-subsistence, may He be exalted, means: He does not depend on a substrate nor a specifier. It means: that it is necessary for Him, may He be exalted, to subsist by Himself (1); i.e., by His essence. And the meaning of His self-subsistence, may He be exalted, is: the negation of His need for anything from among things. So He does not depend, may He be exalted, on a substrate; i.e., an essence other than His essence in which He exists, just as an attribute exists in the described; because that is only for attributes, and He, may He be exalted, is an essence described by attributes, and He is not, glorious and majestic, an attribute, as the Christians and those like them from the Batinis claim—may Allah destroy them all—and the proof of that will come, if Allah wills, when we treat the proofs (2). And likewise He does not depend, may He be exalted, on a specifier; i.e., an agent that specifies Him with existence, neither in His essence nor in any of His attributes, due to the necessity of pre-eternity and everlastingness for His essence, may He be exalted, and for all His attributes. Only one who accepts non-existence needs the specifier—i.e., the agent—and our Master, glorious and majestic, does not accept it. Therefore, dependence is impossible for our Master, glorious and majestic, in general. And by this you know: that our meaning of 'substrate' in creed is essence, and our meaning of 'specifier' is the agent. So by His not depending on a substrate—i.e., another essence—it follows that He, glorious and majestic, is an essence, not an attribute. And by His not depending on a specifier—i.e., an agent—it follows that His supreme essence, glorious and majestic, is not like other essences that also do not depend on a substrate, like bodies for example; because these, even if they are independent of a substrate—i.e., of an essence in which they subsist—they are dependent, initially and perpetually, with a necessary and inseparable dependence on the specifier—i.e., the agent—who is our Master, glorious and majestic. Therefore, self-subsistence is an expression of absolute independence, and that can only be for our Master, blessed and exalted. He said, glorious is He who says: 'O mankind, you are the ones in need of Allah, while Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Praiseworthy' [Fatir 15]. And He said, may He be exalted: 'Allah, the Eternal Refuge. He neither begets nor is born, nor is there to Him any equivalent' [al-Ikhlas 2-4]. So He established, may He be exalted, by His saying, 'Allah, the Eternal Refuge,' the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, glorious and majestic; for al-Samad is the one to whom one turns in needs—i.e., is sought for them—and from whom one asks. And there is no doubt that everything other than Him, may He be exalted, is turning to Him—i.e., dependent on Him initially and perpetually—by the tongue of its state, or by the tongue of its speech, or by both together.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the divine attribute of self-subsistence (al-qiyam bi al-nafs). The author begins by stating that God's self-subsistence means He depends on neither a substrate (mahall) nor a specifier (mukhassis). A substrate is a subject in which something inheres, like an attribute in an essence; a specifier is an agent that brings something into existence. The author explains that God must subsist by His own essence, which means He has no need for anything. He then clarifies the two negations: First, God does not depend on a substrate—an essence other than His own in which He would exist—because only attributes inhere in substrates. Therefore, God is an essence, not an attribute, refuting Christians and Batinis who liken Him to an attribute. Second, God does not depend on a specifier (an agent) that brings Him into existence, because that would imply He was once non-existent. Pre-eternity and everlastingness are necessary for His essence and attributes, so He cannot have a beginning. The author notes that only that which can cease to exist needs an agent to bring it into being. Since God does not accept non-existence, dependence on an agent is impossible for Him. The author then clarifies the technical terms: 'substrate' in creed means 'essence', and 'specifier' means 'agent'. By negating dependence on a substrate, we affirm that God is an essence, not an attribute. By negating dependence on a specifier, we affirm that His essence is not like other self-subsistent entities (e.g., bodies) that, while independent of a substrate, still depend on God as their originating agent. Thus, self-subsistence is absolute independence, belonging only to God. Finally, the author provides Quranic evidence: verse 35:15 establishes that all people are in need of God, and God is the Self-Sufficient (al-Ghani). Verse 112:2-4 describes God as al-Samad (the Eternal Refuge), which implies that all others are directed to Him in need, i.e., dependent on Him—by their very nature (state), by their speech, or both.

Key Terms
القيام بالنفس
المحل
المخصص
الصمد
الغنى المطلق
النصارى
الباطنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'self-subsistence' means God is a substance or subject like physical things, or that He exists independently of a cause but still inheres in something.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that self-subsistence means God depends on neither a substrate (i.e., He is not an attribute in something else) nor a specifier (i.e., He was not brought into existence by an agent). This absolute independence is unique to God.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'self-subsistence' (al-qiyam bi al-nafs) according to Sanusi?
A) That God exists without beginning but depends on a substrate
B) That God is an attribute inhering in a subject
C) That God depends on neither a substrate nor a specifier
D) That God is like a body that does not depend on a substrate but depends on an agent

Key Takeaway
Self-subsistence means God is absolutely independent: He exists by Himself, needing no place to exist (no substrate) and no cause to bring Him into being (no specifier).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God is absolutely independent and you are utterly dependent on Him for every moment of your existence, how would your daily worries and anxieties change? What would you start doing differently today to live in that awareness?
?
Sanusi states that everything other than God depends on Him 'by the tongue of its state.' When you look at your own life, do you sense that your very existence is a constant declaration of need for God? Or have you fallen into the illusion of self-sufficiency? Pause and ask yourself: in what area of your life are you most likely to forget your absolute need for Him? Write down one specific step you can take to remind yourself of your poverty before Him.
?
The lesson refutes the idea that God is like an attribute or depends on anything. How does your understanding of God's self-subsistence affect your worship? Do you pray as if you are truly in need of Him, or do you go through the motions? Commit to one prayer today where you fully realize your dependence on al-Samad.

The Scriptural Proof for Allah's Self-Subsistence
Sanusi expounds on two Qur'anic verses to prove Allah's self-subsistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two Qur'anic verses (Fatir 35:15 and Ikhlas 112:2-4) prove that Allah is absolutely self-sufficient and independent of all causes and effects, and that every other being is in need of Him.

Core Idea
Allah alone is self-sufficient; all creation is needy.

Sanusi presents scriptural proofs for Allah's attribute of self-subsistence. He quotes two powerful verses and unpacks their meanings to show that Allah is the only independent being, while everything else depends on Him for its existence and needs. This lesson will walk through these proofs and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses and translation
Read the Arabic verses from Surah Fatir and Surah Ikhlas, along with their literal translations. Notice the key terms: al-Ghaniyy (Self-Sufficient) and al-Samad (the Self-Sufficient to whom all turn).
2
Understand the meaning of al-Samad
Sanusi explains that al-Samad means the One who is sought in all needs. This implies that every other being is in need of Him, both initially and perpetually.
3
Grasp the negation of cause and effect
From 'lam yalid wa lam yulad', Sanusi derives that Allah has no cause for His existence (lam yulad) and no effect that implies dependency (lam yalid). Understand the implications for tawhid.
4
Reflect on Allah's absolute uniqueness
Sanusi concludes that Allah has no parent, no spouse, no offspring, and no similarity with any contingent being. Reflect on how this establishes His complete otherness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالَ جلَّ مِنْ قائل : يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ أَنتُمُ الْفُقَرَاء إِلَى اللَّهِ وَاللهُ هُوَ الْغَنِيُّ الْحَمِيدُ [فاطر : ١٥] . وقال تعالى : ( اللهُ الصَّمَدُ * لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ * وَلَمْ يَكُن لَهُ كُفُوًا أَحَدٌ [الإخلاص : ٢-٤] ، فأثبت تعالى بقوله : والله الصَّمَدُ افْتِقَارَ كلِّ ما سواه إليهِ جلَّ وعزَّ ؛ إذ الصمد هو الذي يُصمَدُ إليه في الحوائج ؛ أي: يُقصد فيها ، ومنه تُسألُ ، ولا شكَّ أَنَّ كلَّ ما سواه تعالى صامدٌ إِليه ؛ أي : مفتقر إليه ابتداءً ودواماً ؛ بلسان حالِهِ ، أو بلسان مقاله ، أو بهما معاً
وأثبت تعالى بقولِهِ : لَمْ يَلِدْ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ وجوبَ الْغِناءِ لَهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ عن المؤثر والأثرِ ؛ فلا حاجةَ اللهِ تعالى إلى المؤثر ، ولا علة لوجودِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ ، وإليه الإشارة بقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ وَلَمْ يُولَدْ أي : لا يتولد وجوده تعالى عن شيءٍ ؛ أي : لا سبب لوجودِهِ تعالى ؛ لِوُجُوبِ قِدَمِهِ وَبَقَائِهِ • وكذلك لا حاجة لهُ تعالى إلى الأثرِ ؛ وهو ما أوجد تعالى مِنَ الحوادث ، ولا غرضَ لهُ جلَّ وعزَّ في شيء منها ، تعالى ربنا عن الأعراض والأغراض ، ولا معينَ لهُ تعالى في شيء منها ، بل هو جلَّ وعزَّ فاعل بمحض الاختيار بلا واسطة ولا معالجة ولا علة ، وإليهِ الإشارة بقولِهِ تعالى : لَمْ يَلِدْ ﴾ أي : لم يتولَّد وجود شيء عن ذاتِهِ العليَّةِ ؛ بأنْ يكونَ بعضاً منها ، أو ناشئاً عنها مِنْ غير قصد ، أو ناشئاً عنه تعالى باستعانة ممَّنْ يزاوجُهُ على ذلكَ (۱) ، أو ثَمَّ غرضُ يحمله على ذلك كما هو شأن الزوجين ونحوهما بالنسبة إلى الولد ونحوه في جميع ما ذُكِرَ ؛ إذ لو كان تعالى كذلك لزم أن يماثل الحوادث ، كيف وهو تبارك وتعالى ليس له كفواً أحدٌ ؟!
فلا والد إذاً ولا صاحبة ولا ولد ، ولا مماثلة بينه وبين الحوادث
بوجهِ مِنَ الوجوه ، فتباركَ اللهُ ربُّ العالمينَ .
(۱) قوله : ( ممن يزاوجه ) أي : يعاونه . « جمل » ( ق۲۲ ) .
He, may He be glorified, said: 'O mankind, you are the poor toward Allah, and Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Praiseworthy' [Fatir 35:15]. And He, may He be exalted, said: 'Allah, the Self-Sufficient. He begets not nor was He begotten. And there is none comparable to Him' [al-Ikhlas 112:2-4]. So He, may He be exalted, proved by His saying 'and Allah is the Self-Sufficient' the poverty of everything other than Him, may He be glorified and exalted, to Him; for al-Samad is the One who is sought in needs, i.e., intended in them, and from Him they are asked. And there is no doubt that everything other than Him, may He be exalted, is turning toward Him, i.e., in need of Him initially and perpetually, by the tongue of its state, or the tongue of its speech, or both together. And He, may He be exalted, proved by His saying 'He begets not nor was He begotten' the necessity of independence for Him, may He be glorified and exalted, from the cause (mu'aththir) and the effect (athar). So Allah, may He be exalted, has no need of a cause, nor is there a cause for His existence, may He be glorified and exalted. And to this is the reference in His saying, may He be exalted: 'nor was He begotten', i.e., His existence, may He be exalted, does not come into being from anything; i.e., there is no cause for His existence, may He be exalted, because of the necessity of His pre-eternity and everlastingness. Likewise, He, may He be exalted, has no need of the effect (athar), which is what He, may He be exalted, brings into existence of contingent things. And He, may He be glorified and exalted, has no purpose in any of them—exalted is our Lord above accidents and purposes. Nor does He have any helper in any of them. Rather, He, may He be glorified and exalted, is an agent by pure choice, without any intermediary, effort, or cause. And to this is the reference in His saying, may He be exalted: 'He begets not', i.e., no thing's existence has come into being from His sublime essence—whether it be a part of it, or arising from it without intent, or arising from Him, may He be exalted, with the assistance of someone co operating with Him in that, or there being a purpose driving Him to that as is the case with spouses and the like regarding offspring and the like in all that was mentioned; for if He, may He be exalted, were like that, it would necessitate that He resemble contingencies. How is that when He, may He be blessed and exalted, has none comparable to Him? So there is no parent, no consort, no offspring, and no similarity between Him and contingencies in any way. So blessed is Allah, Lord of the worlds. (1) His statement: 'with someone co operating with him', i.e., assisting him. 'Jumal' (Q22).
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof for the divine attribute of self-subsistence (qiyam bi nafs) using two key Qur'anic verses. The author first quotes Surah Fatir 35:15, which declares that all people are poor toward Allah while Allah is the Self-Sufficient (al-Ghaniyy). He then quotes Surah al-Ikhlas 112:2-4, which describes Allah as al-Samad (the Self-Sufficient) and negates that He begets or is begotten, and negates any likeness to Him. The author explains the meaning of al-Samad: the One to whom all turn in need, from whom all needs are sought. Every other being is 'sāmid ilayh' (turning to Him), i.e., in need of Him initially and perpetually. Next, he explains the phrase 'lam yalid wa lam yulad' (He begets not nor was He begotten) as proving Allah's independence from both cause (mu'aththir) and effect (athar). 'Lam yulad' negates any cause for His existence, affirming His eternal necessity. 'Lam yalid' negates any effect proceeding from Him in a way that would entail composition, division, or dependency—whether as a part, or spontaneously, or with assistance, or for a purpose. All such would imply resemblance to contingent beings. The author concludes by affirming the absolute uniqueness of Allah: no parent, spouse, offspring, or similarity.

الغني
الفقير
المؤثر
الأثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'lam yalid wa lam yulad' only negates physical birth, but it negates any causal relationship or dependency whatsoever.
Correction: Sanusi explains that these phrases negate any cause for Allah's existence and any effect that implies dependency, including being a part, arising spontaneously, with assistance, or for a purpose.

Key Takeaway
Allah's self-subsistence means He is independent of all causes and effects, and everything else depends entirely on Him.

The Three Aspects of God's Oneness
Sanusi defines الوحدانية and enumerates its three aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three aspects of God's oneness as defined by Sanusi: negation of multiplicity in essence, negation of an equal, and exclusive creative power.

Core Idea
God's oneness has three dimensions: no internal parts, no equal, and sole creative power.

Sanusi unpacks the meaning of God's oneness (الوحدانية) into three precise aspects. Before studying this passage, many think of oneness simply as 'one God'. But Sanusi shows it covers essence, attributes, and actions. This lesson will walk through each aspect and the Quranic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi defines الوحدانية before listing its three aspects.
2
Identify the three aspects
The passage presents three distinct aspects of God's oneness. Find each one and notice the terms used: الكم المتصل, الكم المنفصل, and الانفراد بالإيجاد والتدبير.
These correspond to no internal multiplicity, no equal, and exclusive creative control.
3
Reflect on the Quranic proofs
Sanusi supports the third aspect with four Quranic verses. Read them and consider how they affirm that only God creates and manages everything.
The verses emphasize God's sole creative power and authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صفة الوحدانية وَالْوَحْدَانِيَّةُ؛ أَيْ: لَا ثَانِيَ لَهُ فِي ذَاتِهِ، وَلَا فِي صِفَاتِهِ، وَلَا فِي أَفْعَالِهِ. يعني: أنَّ الوحدانية في حقه تعالى تشتمل على ثلاثة أوجه: أحدها: نفْيُ الكثرةِ في ذاتِهِ تعالى، ويُسمَّى: الكم المتصل. الثاني: نفْيُّ النظير له جلَّ وعزَّ في ذاتِهِ تعالى أو في صفةٍ مِنْ صفاته، ويُسمى: الكم المنفصل. الثالثُ: انفراده تعالى بالإيجادِ والتدبير العام بلا واسطة ولا معالجة، فلا مؤثر سواهُ تعالى في أثر ما عموماً، قالَ جلَّ مِنْ قائل: ﴿ إِنَّا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقْتَهُ بِقَدَرٍ ﴾ [القمر: 49]، وقال تعالى: ﴿ ذَلِكُمُ اللَّهُ رَبُّكُمْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ خَلِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ فَاعْبُدُوهُ ﴾ [الأنعام: 102]، وقال جل وعزّ: لَهُ مُلْكُ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ [الحديد: 2]، وقال تبارك وتعالى: ﴿ وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: 96].
The Attribute of Oneness (al-Waḥdāniyyah): meaning: there is no second to Him in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His actions. That is: the Oneness with respect to Him, exalted, comprises three aspects: The first: negation of multiplicity in His essence, exalted, and it is called: continuous quantity (al-kamm al-muttaṣil). The second: negation of an equal to Him, exalted and majestic, in His essence, exalted, or in any of His attributes, and it is called: discrete quantity (al-kamm al-munfaṣil). The third: His exclusive uniqueness, exalted, in origination and universal management without intermediacy or labor, so there is no effective cause besides Him, exalted, in any effect universally. He said, exalted: 'Indeed, We have created everything in a determined measure' (Quran 54:49); and He said, exalted: 'That is God, your Lord; there is no deity except Him, the Creator of all things, so worship Him' (Quran 6:102); and He said, exalted and majestic: 'To Him belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth' (Quran 57:2); and He said, blessed and exalted: 'And God created you and what you do' (Quran 37:96).
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of Oneness (الوحدانية) as the negation of a second in essence, attributes, and actions. Sanusi then breaks it down into three aspects. The first is the negation of multiplicity within God's essence; this is called continuous quantity (الكم المتصل), meaning no internal composition. The second is the negation of any peer or equal to God in essence or attributes; this is called discrete quantity (الكم المنفصل), meaning no external equal. The third aspect is God's exclusive uniqueness in origination and universal management without any intermediary or effort, meaning that no other being is an effective cause in any effect; God alone is the sole creator and sustainer. He supports this with Quranic verses: everything is created by God's decree, God is the Creator of all things, His is the dominion, and He created people and their actions.

Key Terms
وحدانية
كم متصل
كم منفصل
نظير
انفراد بالإيجاد
تدبير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's oneness only means numerical oneness (there is one God).
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that oneness includes not only numerical unity, but also no internal parts, no equal, and exclusive creative power.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does 'الكم المنفصل' refer to in the context of God's oneness?
A) Negation of multiplicity in essence
B) Negation of an equal to God in essence or attributes
C) God's exclusive creation
D) God's universal management

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's definition of God's oneness goes beyond mere numerical unity to include no internal multiplicity, no equal, and sole creative power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your daily successes and failures, do you genuinely believe that no other being—your boss, your health, or even your own effort—has any independent effect? How would your level of trust in God change if you internalized that every cause is a mere instrument for His exclusive action?
?
Reflect on your own pride in your qualities like intelligence or kindness. If God has no equal in His attributes, then your attributes are not your own possessions. In what specific area do you need to stop taking credit and acknowledge that you are simply a vessel for God's attributes?
?
You end your prayers with 'assalamu alaykum,' but do you ever feel a subtle fear of other people's opinions or power? How does Sanusi's third aspect—that no effective cause exists besides God—confront that fear, and what would it mean for you to live today as if only God's will truly matters?

The Three Aspects of Divine Oneness
Enumeration of the three aspects of divine Oneness with scriptural proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct aspects of divine Oneness according to Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Divine Oneness covers essence, attributes, and actions—three inseparable facets.

This passage from Sanusi's creed defines the attribute of Oneness (al-waḥdāniyya) by breaking it into three clear aspects. Before reading, note that this goes beyond simply saying 'there is no god but Allah'—it specifies how Allah is one in His essence, in His attributes, and in His actions. Let's explore each aspect as the author presents them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Let the rhythm of the definitions and verses sink in.
Notice the three numbered aspects.
2
Identify the three categories
Find each of the three aspects: continuous quantum, discrete quantum, and exclusivity in creation. Pay attention to how each is defined.
3
Connect the verses
Look at the four Quranic verses cited. How does each support the aspect of exclusivity?
The verses are from Al-Qamar, Al-An'am, Al-Hadid, and As-Saffat.
4
Reflect on the misconception
The common misunderstanding is that oneness only means no partner in worship. How does this passage expand that?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صِفَةُ الْوَحْدَانِيَّةِ وَالْوَحْدَانِيَّةُ ؛ أَيْ : لا ثَانِيَ لَهُ فِي ذَاتِهِ ، وَلَا فِي صِفَاتِهِ ، وَلَا فِي أَفْعَالِهِ يَعْنِي : أَنَّ الْوَحْدَانِيَّةَ فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى تَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةِ أَوْجُهٍ : أَحَدُهَا : نَفْيُ الْكُثْرَةِ فِي ذَاتِهِ تَعَالَى ، وَيُسَمَّى : الْكَمَّ الْمُتَّصِلَ الثَّانِي : نَفْيُ النَّظِيرِ لَهُ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ فِي ذَاتِهِ تَعَالَى أَوْ فِي صِفَةٍ مِنْ صِفَاتِهِ ، وَيُسَمَّى : الْكَمَّ الْمُنْفَصِلَ الثَّالِثُ : انْفِرَادُهُ تَعَالَى بِالْإِيجَادِ وَالتَّدْبِيرِ الْعَامِّ بِلَا وَاسِطَةٍ وَلَا مُعَالَجَةٍ ، فَلَا مُؤَثِّرَ سِوَاهُ تَعَالَى فِي أَثَرٍ مَا عُمُومًا ، قَالَ جَلَّ مِنْ قَائِلٍ : ﴿ إِنَّا كُلَّ شَيْءٍ خَلَقْنَاهُ بِقَدَرٍ ﴾ [القمر : ٤٩] ، وَقَالَ تَعَالَى : ﴿ ذَلِكُمُ اللَّهُ رَبُّكُمْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ خَالِقُ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ فَاعْبُدُوهُ ﴾ [الأنعام : ١٠٢] ، وَقَالَ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ : ﴿ لَهُ مُلْكُ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ ﴾ [الحديد : ٢] ، وَقَالَ تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى : ﴿ وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات : ٩٦] .
The attribute of Oneness. And Oneness means: there is no second to Him in His essence, nor in His attributes, nor in His actions. It means that Oneness in His right, exalted is He, includes three aspects: First: negating multiplicity in His essence, exalted is He, and it is called the continuous quantum. Second: negating an equal to Him, majestic and mighty, in His essence, exalted is He, or in any of His attributes, and it is called the discrete quantum. Third: His exclusivity, exalted is He, in origination and universal management without intermediary or treatment, so there is no effecter besides Him, exalted is He, in any effect whatsoever, universally. He, majestic is He who speaks, said: {Indeed, all things We created by decree} (Al-Qamar 49); and He, exalted is He, said: {That is Allah, your Lord; there is no deity except Him, the Creator of all things, so worship Him} (Al-An'am 102); and He, majestic and mighty, said: {To Him belongs the dominion of the heavens and the earth} (Al-Hadid 2); and He, blessed and exalted, said: {And Allah created you and what you do} (As-Saffat 96).
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of Oneness (الوحدانية) and explains its three constituent aspects. The author first states the core meaning: no second to Allah in essence, attributes, or actions. Then he explicates three aspects:
1. Continuous quantum (الكم المتصل): negating multiplicity within the divine essence — Allah's essence is not composed of parts.
2. Discrete quantum (الكم المنفصل): negating any equal or counterpart to Allah in essence or attributes — no one shares His essential or attribute perfections.
3. Exclusivity in origination and management: Allah alone creates and governs all things universally, without intermediaries or effort. No other being has any independent effect. To support this, the author cites four Quranic verses: (Al-Qamar 49), (Al-An'am 102), (Al-Hadid 2), and (As-Saffat 96), all affirming Allah's sole creative power and dominion.

Key Terms
الوحدانية
الكم المتصل
الكم المنفصل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that divine Oneness only means no partner in worship (tawḥīd al-ulūhiyya) without including oneness of essence and attributes.
Correction: This passage shows that oneness also negates multiplicity in essence and any equal in attributes, expanding tawḥīd beyond worship alone.

Checkpoint

B) Three

Key Takeaway
Divine Oneness encompasses three inseparable aspects: unity of essence, unity of attributes, and unity of actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The continuous quantum says Allah has no parts. Have you ever unconsciously imagined Allah in human terms—with a body, location, or limitations—even while knowing He is beyond that? What steps will you take to purify your mental image of Allah based on this lesson?

The Essential and Negative Attributes of Allah
Enumerates six attributes and defines the essential attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the essential attribute (al-wujud) and how it differs from attributes of meaning (al-ma'nawiyyah) and the accidental realities themselves.

Core Idea
The essential attribute is uncaused and inseparable from the essence, unlike attributes that depend on cause.

Sanusi begins the examination of divine attributes by distinguishing six categories. The first, the essential attribute, is existence itself—a state that necessarily accompanies the essence without any cause. This lesson unpacks that definition and shows why it excludes attributes like knowledge and power, which are caused by underlying realities subsisting in the essence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six attributes
Read the passage and note that the first attribute is essential (nafsiyyah) and it is existence; the remaining five are negative (salbiyyah).
2
Understand the definition of essential attribute
Focus on the definition: it is a state necessarily belonging to the essence as long as the essence endures, not caused by a cause. Contrast with the example of a body occupying space.
The phrase 'not caused by a cause' is crucial.
3
Differentiate from attributes of meaning
Notice how Sanusi uses the condition 'not caused by a cause' to exclude attributes like being knowing, powerful, or willing, which are caused by the subsistence of knowledge, power, and will.
Knowledge and power themselves are not essential or meaning attributes; they are states (ahwal) that are not existent entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَهَذِهِ سِتُّ صِفَاتٍ ، الْأُولَى نَفْسِيَّةٌ ؛ وَهِيَ الْوُجُودُ ، وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبِيَّةٌ . حَقِيقَةُ الصِّفَةِ النَّفْسِيَّةِ : هِيَ الْحَالُ الْوَاجِبَةُ لِلذَّاتِ مَا دَامَتِ الذَّاتُ غَيْرَ مُعَلَّلَةٍ بِعِلَّةٍ (١) ؛ كَالتَّحَيُّزِ لِلْجِرْمِ مَثَلًا (٢) ؛ فَإِنَّهُ وَاجِبٌ لِلْجِرْمِ مَا دَامَ الْجِرْمَ ، وَلَيْسَ ثُبُوتُهُ لَهُ مُعَلَّلًا بِعِلَّةٍ . وَاحْتَرَزَ بِقَوْلِهِ : ( غَيْرَ مُعَلَّلَةٍ بِعِلَّةٍ ) مِنَ الْأَحْوَالِ الْمَعْنَوِيَّةِ؛ كَكَوْنِ الذَّاتِ عَالِمَةً وَقَادِرَةً وَمُرِيدَةً مَثَلًا؛ فَإِنَّهَا مُعَلَّلَةٌ بِقِيَامِ الْعِلْمِ وَالْقُدْرَةِ وَالْإِرَادَةِ بِالذَّاتِ (٣) ، أَمَّا الْعِلْمُ وَالْقُدْرَةُ فَلَيْسَا مِنَ الصِّفَاتِ النَّفْسِيَّةِ وَلَا مِنَ الْمَعْنَوِيَّةِ؛ لِأَنَّ هَاتَيْنِ أَحْوَالٌ، وَالْحَالُ لَيْسَتْ بِمَوْجُودَةٍ فِي (١) قَوْلُهُ : ( غَيْرُ مُعَلَّلَةٍ ) مَنْصُوبٌ عَلَى الْحَالِيَّةِ، لَا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَرُ ( دَامَ ) لِأَنَّهَا هُنَا تَامَّةٌ . (٢) انْظُرِ ( الْإِرْشَادَ ) لِإِمَامِ الْحَرَمَيْنِ ( ص ٣٠ ) ، قَوْلُهُ : ( مَا دَامَتِ الذَّاتُ ) مَا : مَصْدَرِيَّةٌ ظَرْفِيَّةٌ مَعْمُولَةٌ لِقَوْلِهِ : ( الْوَاجِبَةِ لِلذَّاتِ )، وَدَامَ : تَامَّةٌ لَا خَبَرَ لَهَا؛ أَيْ : الْوَاجِبَةُ لِلذَّاتِ مُدَّةَ دَوَامِ الذَّاتِ، وَفِيهِ تَنْبِيهٌ عَلَى أَنَّ الْأَمْرَ النَّفْسِيَّ لَا يَتَخَلَّفُ عَنِ الذَّاتِ الَّتِي ذَلِكَ الْأَمْرُ النَّفْسِيُّ لَهَا، وَلِذَلِكَ يَقُولُونَ : إِنَّ مَا بِالذَّاتِ لَا يَخْتَلِفُ وَلَا يَتَخَلَّفُ . (٣) فِي ( هـ ) زِيَادَةٌ : ( وَاحْتَرَزَ أَيْضًا مِنْ صِفَاتِ الْمَعَانِي )
So these are six attributes: the first is essential (nafsiyyah), and it is existence (al-wujud); the five after it are negative (salbiyyah). The reality of the essential attribute: it is the state necessarily belonging to the essence as long as the essence exists, not caused by a cause; like being in space for a body, for example; for it is necessary for the body as long as it is a body, and its being established for it is not caused by a cause. And he guarded, by his saying: 'not caused by a cause', against the states of meaning (al-ahwal al-ma'nawiyyah), such as the essence being knowing, powerful, and willing, for example; for they are caused by the subsistence of knowledge, power, and will in the essence. As for knowledge and power, they are neither from the essential attributes nor from the attributes of meaning; because these two are states, and the state is not existent in...
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage enumerates the six attributes (the first being essential, the rest negative) and then defines the essential attribute. The author specifies that the essential attribute is 'existence' (al-wujud). The definition: it is a state (hal) that necessarily belongs to the essence as long as the essence endures, and it is not caused by any cause. An example is occupying space (al-tahayyuz) for a body—it is intrinsic to the body without a cause. The phrase 'not caused by a cause' excludes the 'states of meaning' (al-ahwal al-ma'nawiyyah) like being knowing, powerful, or willing, which depend on accidental realities (knowledge, power, will) subsisting in the essence. The author further clarifies that knowledge and power themselves are not essential attributes nor attributes of meaning, because they are states (ahwal), and the state is not an existent entity. The footnote provides grammatical analysis and notes that the essential is always concomitant with the essence and never differs or lags.

Key Terms
الصفة النفسية
الصفات السلبية
الوجود
الحال
المعنى
الصفة المعنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the essential attribute is like attributes of meaning, i.e., caused by something else.
Correction: The essential attribute is uncaused and necessarily accompanies the essence without any cause, unlike attributes of meaning which depend on accident realities.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The essential attribute (existence) is an uncaused state that necessarily belongs to Allah's essence, distinguishing it from all other attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's existence is uncaused and necessary, how does that challenge your dependence on created causes for your sense of security? What in your life do you mistakenly treat as necessary that only Allah's uncaused existence can provide?
?
The essential attribute is not separate from Allah's essence—it is a state that cannot be removed. Do you ever think of Allah's attributes as if they are added to Him, making Him seem composed? How should this affect your worship and trust in His oneness?
?
Sanusi distinguishes between uncaused states (essential) and caused states (attributes of meaning). Which of your own states (moods, beliefs, inclinations) do you treat as uncaused and permanent, when they are actually caused and temporary? How can you realign your self-awareness to reflect this truth?

The Self-Attribute: Definition and Distinctions
Sanusi defines the self-attribute and clarifies related distinctions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the self-attribute and how it differs from modal attributes and attributes of meanings.

Core Idea
A self-attribute is a necessary state of the essence, uncaused by any separate attribute.

Sanusi begins by identifying six attributes, the first being the self-attribute of existence. He carefully defines what makes an attribute 'self-attribute' and distinguishes it from other types. This lesson unpacks his definition and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of self-attribute
Locate the sentence defining the self-attribute and note its key components: state, necessary, uncaused.
2
Understand the distinction from modal attributes
See how modal attributes are caused by separate attributes like knowledge, while self-attribute is not.
3
Consider the status of existence
Note Sanusi's discussion that existence is considered self-attribute only if one holds it as additional; otherwise it is identical to essence.
This connects to a prior discussion about counting existence as an attribute.
4
Apply the concept
Reflect on why this distinction matters for understanding God's essence.

فَهَذِهِ سِتْ صِفَاتٍ، الأُولَى نَفْسِيَّةٌ؛ وَهِيَ الْوُجُودُ، وَالْخَمْسَةُ بَعْدَهَا سَلْبيَّةٌ. حقيقة الصفة النفسية: هي الحالُ الواجبة للذاتِ ما دامَتِ الذاتُ غير معللة بعلَّةٍ؛ كالتحيز للجرم مثلاً؛ فإنَّهُ واجبٌ للجرمِ ما دامَ الجرم، وليس ثبوته له معللاً بعلة. واحترزَ بقولِهِ: (غير معلَّلة بعلَّةٍ) مِنَ الأحوال المعنويَّةِ؛ ككونِ الذاتِ عالمة وقادرة ومريدة مثلاً؛ فإنَّها معللة بقيام العلم والقدرةِ والإرادة بالذات. أمَّا العلم والقدرة فليسا مِنَ الصفات النفسية ولا مِنَ المعنويَّةِ؛ لأنَّ هاتين أحوال، والحالُ ليسَتْ بموجودة في نفسها ولا معدومة، والعلم والقدرة صفتان موجودتان في أنفسهما، قائمتان بموجود. فإذا عرفت هذا فاعلم: أنَّ (الوجودَ) إِنَّما يصحُ أنْ يكونَ صفةً نفسيَّةً عندَ مَنْ يجعلُهُ زائداً على الذاتِ، وأمَّا مَنْ يجعلُه نفسَ الذاتِ فليس بصفةٍ أصلاً، وقد سبق الاعتذار عن عدهِ مِنَ الصفاتِ، وبمثل ذلك يُعتذَرُ هنا عن عدهِ مِنَ الصفات النفسية؛ أي: معنى الوجودِ راجع للذاتِ، سواءٌ قلنا: إِنَّهُ عينُ الذاتِ، أو زائد على حقيقتها؛ لأنَّ الذات لا تثبتُ في الخارج عن الذهنِ إلا أن تكونَ موجودةً. قوله: (والخمسة بعدها سلبيةٌ) يعني: أن مدلول كل واحد منها عدم أمر لا يليق بمولانا جل وعزَّ، وليس مدلولها صفة موجودة في نفسها كما في العلم والقدرة ونحوهما مِنْ سائر صفاتِ المعاني الآتية. قد يقال: وصفات المعاني أيضاً سلبية؛ لأنها تسلب أضدادها؛ فالقدرة مثلاً تسلب عن الله تعالى العجز، وهكذا. والجواب: لا خلاف في كون صفات المعاني سالبة أضدادها عنه سبحانه، ولكن هذا السلب حاصل بقيامها بذاته سبحانه، ولذا نقل العلامة الدسوقي في حاشيته عن المحقق عبد الفتـاح الملوي قولـه: والتحقيق: أن الصفة السلبية مباينة للسالبة؛ لأن السلبية: ما دل لفظها على نفي نقص مطابقةً؛ كالخمسة المذكورة، والسالبة: ما دلّ لفظها على نفي
Thus these are six attributes: the first is self-attribute, which is existence, and the five after it are negative. The reality of the self-attribute: it is the state necessarily belonging to the essence as long as the essence exists, not caused by a cause; like occupying space for a body, for example; for it is necessary for the body as long as the body exists, and its establishment for it is not caused by a cause. And he guarded by his statement 'not caused by a cause' against the modal states; like the essence being knowing, able, and willing, for example; for they are caused by the subsistence of knowledge, power, and will in the essence. As for knowledge and power, they are not among the self-attributes nor among the modal attributes; because these two are states, and the state is neither existent in itself nor non-existent, while knowledge and power are two attributes existent in themselves, subsisting in an existent. So if you know this, then know: that existence is only valid to be a self-attribute for one who makes it additional to the essence; as for one who makes it the essence itself, it is not an attribute at all, and the apology for counting it among the attributes has already preceded; and by a similar [apology] one apologizes here for counting it among the self-attributes; that is, the meaning of existence refers to the essence, whether we say it is identical to the essence or additional to its reality; because the essence is not established in the external mind unless it is existent. His statement: 'and the five after it are negative' means that the signification of each one of them is the negation of what is unbefitting for our Lord, Glorious and Exalted, and their signification is not an attribute existent in itself as in knowledge, power, and the like from the rest of the attributes of meanings to come. It may be said: the attributes of meanings are also negative because they negate their opposites; for example, power negates incapacity from God Most High, and so on. The answer: there is no dispute that the attributes of meanings are negators of their opposites from Him, Exalted, but this negation occurs by their subsistence in His essence. Hence the scholar al-Dasuqi transmitted in his gloss from the investigator Abd al-Fattah al-Malawi his statement: 'The verification is that the negative attribute is different from the negating attribute; because the negative: its word indicates the negation of deficiency by conformity, like the five mentioned, and the negating: its word indicates negation.'
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition and classification passage. Sanusi first identifies six attributes of God: one self-attribute (existence) and five negative attributes (which will be explained later). He then defines the self-attribute as a state that necessarily belongs to the essence as long as the essence exists, without being caused by any cause. This is distinguished from modal attributes (ahwal ma'nawiyya), which are caused by the subsistence of attributes like knowledge, power, and will in the essence. He clarifies that knowledge and power themselves are not states but rather real attributes subsisting in God. Next, he addresses the status of existence as a self-attribute, noting that it is considered self-attribute only if one holds that existence is additional to the essence; if one holds it identical to the essence, it is not an attribute at all, but an apology is made for counting it due to its necessity. The passage then explains that the five attributes after existence are negative, meaning they denote the negation of what is unbefitting for God, not positive attributes like knowledge. An objection is raised that attributes of meanings (like power) also negate opposites (e.g., power negates incapacity), so they are also negative. The answer distinguishes between a negative attribute (sifa salbiyya), which directly negates a deficiency, and a negating attribute (sifa saliba), which negates its opposite indirectly through its positive meaning. Thus, the negative attributes are a separate category.

Key Terms
الصفة النفسية
الحال
المعنوية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that self-attributes and modal attributes are the same.
Correction: Self-attributes are not caused by a separate attribute, while modal attributes are caused by the subsistence of attributes like knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a self-attribute?
A) Existence
B) Knowledge
C) Power
D) Will

Key Takeaway
The self-attribute is a necessary, uncaused state of the essence, exemplified by existence.

Negative Attributes: Definition and Distinction from Negating Attributes
Sanusi explains negative attributes and answers an objection about attributes of meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of negative attributes and how they differ from negating attributes.

Core Idea
Negative attributes directly negate deficiencies; negating attributes negate opposites through positive meaning.

After establishing the self-attribute of existence, Sanusi introduces the five negative attributes. He explains that they signify the negation of what is unbefitting for God, not positive qualities. An important objection is raised and answered, clarifying the difference between negative and negating attributes. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of negative attributes
Find where Sanusi says the five after existence are negative and what that means.
2
Understand the objection
Note the claim that attributes of meanings also negate opposites, so they could be seen as negative.
3
Study the answer
Sanusi distinguishes negative attributes (direct negation of deficiency) from negating attributes (indirect negation via positive meaning).
The quote from al-Dasuqi reinforces this.
4
Apply the distinction
Reflect on why this distinction is important for understanding God's attributes correctly.
