Key Takeaway
Attributing animal-like sounds to God's speech is not just inaccurate but a profound insult, because God's speech transcends all created perfection.

Opposites of the Meaning Attributes
Sanusi lists the opposites of the seven meaning attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical opposites of the seven meaning attributes and why they cannot apply to Allah.

Core Idea
Each meaning attribute has a specific opposite that negates its perfection.

In this passage, Sanusi clarifies the opposites of the seven meaning attributes (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya). These opposites are not mere antonyms but precise logical negations that help us understand what Allah is not. By learning these, we deepen our grasp of tanzih (declaring Allah free from imperfection).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice how Sanusi systematically pairs each attribute with its opposite.
The pattern is: 'the opposite of X is Y' for each attribute.
2
Identify the seven attributes and their opposites
List each meaning attribute and the opposite given. Observe that the opposite is a specific deficiency.
For example, opposite of power is inability, opposite of will is aversion, etc.
3
Understand the logical rule
Sanusi begins by stating that the opposites are 'clear from this'—meaning once you know the attribute, its opposite becomes evident. The opposite is the negation of the attribute's perfection in a specific way.
This is a fundamental principle in kalam: affirming an attribute necessarily negates its opposite.
4
Reflect on why these opposites cannot apply to Allah
Each opposite is a deficiency. Since Allah is perfect, none of these opposites can be attributed to Him. This reinforces tanzih.
For example, Allah cannot be ignorant, dead, deaf, blind, mute, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَضْدَادُ الصِّفَاتِ الْمَعْنَوِيَّةِ وَاضِحَةٌ مِنْ هَذِهِ يَعْنِي: إِذَا عَرَفْتَ كَوْنَ ضِدَّ الْقُدْرَةِ الْعَامَّةِ الْعَجْزَ عَنْ مُمْكِنٍ مَا، لَزِمَ أَنْ يَكُونَ ضِدُّ الصِّفَةِ الْمَعْنَوِيَّةِ اللَّازِمَةِ لِلْقُدْرَةِ - وَهِيَ كَوْنُهُ تَعَالَى قَادِرًا عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْمُمْكِنَاتِ - كَوْنَهُ عَاجِزًا عَنْ مُمْكِنٍ مَا، وَضِدُّ كَوْنِهِ تَعَالَى مُرِيدًا كَوْنَهُ كَارِهًا لِلْفِعْلِ؛ أَيْ: غَيْرَ مُرِيدٍ لَهُ مَعَ إِيجَادِهِ لَهُ، أَوْ كَوْنَهُ يَفْعَلُ فِعْلًا بِالتَّعْلِيلِ أَوِ الطَّبْعِ أَوِ الذُّهُولِ أَوِ الْغَفْلَةِ، وَضِدُّ كَوْنِهِ تَعَالَى عَالِمًا كَوْنَهُ جَاهِلًا أَوْ مَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ بِمَعْلُومٍ مَا، وَضِدُّ كَوْنِهِ تَعَالَى حَيًّا كَوْنَهُ مَيْتًا، وَضِدُّ كَوْنِهِ تَعَالَى سَمِيعًا كَوْنَهُ أَصَمَّ؛ أَيْ: يَغِيبُ عَنْ سَمْعِهِ مَوْجُودٌ مَا، وَضِدُّ كَوْنِهِ تَعَالَى بَصِيرًا كَوْنَهُ أَعْمَى؛ أَيْ: يَغِيبُ عَنْ بَصَرِهِ مَوْجُودٌ مَا، وَضِدُّ كَوْنِهِ تَعَالَى مُتَكَلِّمًا كَوْنَهُ أَبْكَمَ؛ أَيْ: يَقْصُرُ كَلَامُهُ عَنْ مَعْلُومٍ مَا، أَوْ كَوْنَهُ تَعَالَى مُتَكَلِّمًا بِالْحُرُوفِ وَالْأَصْوَاتِ، أَوْ كَوْنَهُ سَاكِتًا عَنْ مَعْلُومٍ مَا.
And the opposites of the meaning attributes are clear from this. That is: when you know that the opposite of general power is inability regarding some possible thing, it follows that the opposite of the meaning attribute necessary for power—which is that He is powerful over all possible things—is that He is unable regarding some possible thing. And the opposite of His being willing is His being averse to the action; i.e., not willing it while bringing it into existence, or His performing an action by causation, nature, heedlessness, or negligence. And the opposite of His being knowing is His being ignorant or something in its meaning regarding some known thing. And the opposite of His being living is His being dead. And the opposite of His being hearing is His being deaf; i.e., some existing thing being absent from His hearing. And the opposite of His being seeing is His being blind; i.e., some existing thing being absent from His sight. And the opposite of His being speaking is His being mute; i.e., His speech falling short of some known thing, or His being speaking with letters and sounds, or His being silent regarding some known thing.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-classification passage where the author lists the opposites of the seven meaning attributes (ṣifāt ma‘nawiyya). The author begins by stating that the opposites are clear from the previous discussion (presumably of the attributes themselves). He then uses the example of the opposite of 'general power' (qudra ‘āmma) to establish the method: the opposite of the attribute is the negation of its perfection in a specific way. For each meaning attribute, he gives its opposite: for being powerful (qādir) it is inability (‘ajz) regarding some possible thing; for being willing (murīd) it is aversion (karh) or acting by causation, nature, heedlessness, or negligence; for being knowing (‘ālim) it is ignorance (jahl) or its equivalent; for being living (ḥayy) it is death (mawt); for being hearing (samī‘) it is deafness (ṣamam); for being seeing (baṣīr) it is blindness (‘amā); for being speaking (mutakallim) it is muteness (bakam), or speaking with letters and sounds, or silence (sukūt). The author is careful to define each opposite in a way that negates the perfection of the attribute while affirming that God is free from any such deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'opposite' here means a coexisting attribute, rather than a logical negation that cannot apply to God.
Correction: These opposites are logical negations of the attribute's perfection. They do not coexist with the attribute; rather, affirming the attribute necessitates denying its opposite.

Checkpoint
What is the opposite of God's attribute of being 'knowing' ('ālim) according to this passage?
A) Being ignorant (jāhil) or something equivalent regarding some known thing
B) Being forgetful (nāsin)
C) Being doubtful (shākk)
D) Being asleep (nā'im)

Key Takeaway
Each meaning attribute has a specific opposite that is a deficiency, and understanding these opposites helps us affirm Allah's perfection through negation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fail in something, do you ever feel that Allah also lacks power? Read the opposite of power: inability regarding some possible thing. Does that description match your thoughts about Allah? Repent and affirm His complete power.
?
The opposite of His will is aversion or acting ignorantly. In your life, when things don't go your way, do you ever think Allah is unwilling or careless? How does this lesson correct that assumption?
?
The opposite of His hearing is deafness - that some existing thing is absent from His hearing. When you feel unheard in your duas, do you truly believe that not a single sound is absent from His hearing? Or do you doubt? Commit to trusting His perfect hearing.

The Opposites of God's Mental Attributes
Sanusi enumerates the opposites of each mental attribute of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific opposites of each of God's mental attributes as defined by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Every divine mental attribute has a precise opposite that negates it concretely.

Sanusi now completes the picture of God's attributes by listing their opposites. Understanding these opposites is crucial because they clarify what God cannot be—each attribute's negation is defined in specific terms, not vague absence. This passage systematically pairs each mental attribute with its contradictory state.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Sanusi lists each attribute and its opposite in a structured manner.
The passage includes footnotes that clarify the scope of 'general power' and a manuscript variant.
2
Identify each attribute-opposite pair
Go through each pair: power-incapacity, will-aversion, knowledge-ignorance, life-death, hearing-deafness, sight-blindness, speech-muteness. Observe the specific phrasing for each opposite.
3
Understand the precision of definitions
Notice that the opposite of hearing is not just 'not hearing' but 'deafness meaning some existent is absent from His hearing.' This precision is important in kalam.
The opposite is a concrete state that contradicts the attribute's perfection.
4
Generalize the rule
Sanusi concludes: every mental attribute's opposite is the opposite of the mental attribute necessarily connected to it. Reflect on how this pattern applies to all mental attributes.
This is a logical extrapolation from the examples given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَضْدَادُ الصِّفَاتِ الْمَعْنَوِيَّةِ وَاضِحَةٌ مِنْ هَذِهِ
يعني : إذا عرفت كونَ ضدَّ القدرة العامة العجز عن ممكن ما (۱) . لزمَ أنْ يكونَ ضدُّ الصفة المعنوية اللازمة للقدرة - وهي كونُهُ تعالى قادراً على جميع الممكنات - كونه عاجزاً عن ممكن ما ، وضد عن كونه تعالى مريداً كونَهُ كارهاً للفعل ؛ أي : غير مريدٍ لهُ معَ إيجادِهِ له ، أو كونه يفعلُ فعلاً بالتعليل أو الطبع أو الذهول أو الغفلة ، وضد كونه تعالى عالماً كونه جاهلاً أو ما في معناه بمعلوم ما ، وضد كونه تعالى حيّاً كونه ميتاً ، وضدُّ كونه تعالى سميعاً كونه أصم ؛ أي : يغيب عن سمعه موجود ما ، وضدُّ كونه تعالى بصيراً كونه أعمى ؛ أي : يغيب عن بصرِهِ موجود ما ، وضدُّ كونه تعالى متكلّماً كونَهُ أبكم ؛ أي : يقصرُ كلامُهُ عن معلوم ما ، أو كونه تعالى متكلماً بالحروف والأصوات ، أو كونه ساكتاً عن معلوم ما (۲) ،
(۱) قوله : ( العامة ( قيد به ليصح التقابل بينها وبين العجز ، وإلا فبقطع النظر عنه يمكن أن يكون قادراً على شيء وعاجزاً عن آخر ، فلا تقابل ولا تضاد جمل » ( ق۳۸ )
(۲) سقط تفصيل أضداد المعنوية من النسخة ( هـ ) فقط، وأثبت في سائر النسخ
وهكذا كلُّ صفة معنى ؛ فإنَّ ضدَّها ضدُّ للصفة المعنوية اللازمة لها
وبالله تعالى التوفيق
And the opposites of the mental attributes are clear from this. Meaning: if you know that the opposite of the general power is incapacity with respect to some possible thing (1). It follows that the opposite of the mental attribute necessarily connected to power—which is His being powerful over all possibles—is His being incapable of some possible thing. And the opposite of His being willing is His being averse to the act; that is, not willing it while bringing it into existence, or His doing an act by way of causation, nature, absentmindedness, or heedlessness. And the opposite of His being knowing is His being ignorant or something equivalent with respect to some known thing. And the opposite of His being living is His being dead. And the opposite of His being hearing is His being deaf; that is, some existent is absent from His hearing. And the opposite of His being seeing is His being blind; that is, some existent is absent from His sight. And the opposite of His being speaking is His being mute; that is, His speech falls short of some known thing, or His speaking through letters and sounds, or His being silent about some known thing (2). (1) His saying: 'the general' is a qualification to make the correlation between it and incapacity correct; otherwise, apart from that, it is possible that one is powerful over something and incapable of another, so there is no correlation or total opposition. (Q38) (2) The detail of the opposites of the mental attributes is missing from copy (H) only, but it is established in other copies. And thus every mental attribute; its opposite is the opposite of the mental attribute necessarily connected to it. And with Allah Almighty is success.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the opposites (أضداد) of God's mental attributes (الصفات المعنوية). The author begins by stating that these opposites are evident from what has preceded (presumably the definitions of the attributes). He then explains that since the opposite of the general attribute of power (القدرة العامة) is incapacity (العجز) with respect to a possible thing, the opposite of the mental attribute necessarily connected to power—i.e., God's being powerful over all possibles—is His being incapable of some possible thing. For will (الإرادة), the opposite is aversion to the act, which includes not willing an act while still producing it, or doing an act through mechanism, nature, absentmindedness, or heedlessness. For knowledge (العلم), the opposite is ignorance or something similar concerning a known thing. For life (الحياة), the opposite is death. For hearing (السمع), the opposite is deafness (الصمم), meaning some existent is absent from His hearing. For sight (البصر), the opposite is blindness (الأعمى), meaning some existent is absent from His sight. For speech (الكلام), the opposite is muteness (البكم), meaning His speech falls short of some known thing, or that He speaks through letters and sounds, or that He is silent about a known thing. The passage includes two footnotes: one clarifying that 'general' in 'general power' is a qualifier to ensure proper correlation with incapacity, and another noting a manuscript variant where the detail of these opposites is missing in one copy but confirmed in others. The author concludes with a general rule: every mental attribute has an opposite that is the opposite of the mental attribute necessarily connected to it. The passage ends with a supplication for divine assistance.

القدرة
العجز

العلم
الجهل
الحياة

البصر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the opposite of an attribute is simply the lack of that attribute (e.g., not powerful, not knowing).
Correction: Sanusi shows that the opposites are specific contradictory states: e.g., the opposite of hearing is deafness defined as an existent escaping His hearing, not mere absence of hearing.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the opposite of God's attribute of hearing (السمع)?
A) Deafness (الصمم) meaning that some existent is absent from His hearing
B) Inability to hear all sounds

Key Takeaway
The opposites of God's mental attributes are defined as concrete states that negate the attribute's perfection, not merely the absence of the attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God's hearing has no opposite (i.e., He is never deaf to you), how would it change the way you call upon Him in times of distress? What is one instance today where you can act on that belief?

The opposite of God's knowledge is ignorance. Reflect on a moment when you acted as if God were ignorant of your sin. What does this passage tell you about the seriousness of that assumption?
?

The Opposite of a Meaning-Based Attribute
Sanusi states a rule about opposites of meaning-based attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relationship between a meaning-based divine attribute and its opposite, and why this rule is specific to such attributes.

Core Idea
For meaning-based attributes, the opposite directly negates the attribute.

Sanusi closes a discussion on divine attributes with a concise rule: for every meaning-based attribute (sifat ma'nawiyya), its opposite is precisely the negation of that attribute. This lesson unpacks this principle and clarifies its scope, distinguishing it from essential attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Notice the concise style and the concluding phrase.
The phrase 'by Allah Almighty is success' signals the end of a section.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on 'صفة معنى' (meaning-based attribute) and 'ضد' (opposite). Understand that this rule applies specifically to attributes that are not essential but rather derive from meanings.
Meaning-based attributes are those like 'Knowledgeable' or 'Powerful' – they have a conceptual opposite (ignorance, weakness).
3
Understand the relationship
The passage states that the opposite of such an attribute is directly opposite to the attribute itself. For example, the opposite of 'Knowledge' is 'Ignorance', which negates the attribute.
This reinforces that God's attributes are exclusive of their opposites – He cannot have opposing qualities.
4
Review the common misunderstanding
Note that this rule is not a general logical principle for all attributes; it is specific to meaning-based attributes. Essential attributes (like existence) do not have opposites.
The checkpoint will test this understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهكذا كلُّ صفة معنى ؛ فإنَّ ضدَّها ضدُّ للصفة المعنوية اللازمة لها وبالله تعالى التوفيق *
And likewise every attribute of meaning: indeed its opposite is opposite to the necessary meaning-based attribute. And by Allah Almighty is success. *
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a concluding statement about divine attributes, specifically meaning-based attributes (sifat al-ma'nawiyya). The author asserts a general rule: for every such attribute, its opposite (didd) is directly opposite to the attribute itself. For example, if a necessary meaning-based attribute exists, its opposite negates that attribute. This reinforces the principle that God's attributes are exclusive of their opposites. The phrase 'by Allah Almighty is success' indicates the end of a section.

Key Terms
صفة معنى
ضد
الصفة المعنوية اللازمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The rule applies to all divine attributes, including essential ones.
Correction: This rule is specific to meaning-based attributes (e.g., Knowledge, Power) which have conceptual opposites. Essential attributes (e.g., Existence, Divinity) do not have opposites.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the relationship between the opposite of a meaning-based attribute and the attribute itself?
A) The opposite is identical to the attribute.
B) The opposite is opposite to the attribute.
C) The opposite is unrelated.
D) The opposite confirms the attribute.

Key Takeaway
For every meaning-based divine attribute, its opposite directly negates that attribute, affirming that God's attributes are exclusive of their opposites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's knowledge has no opposite such as ignorance, how does that confront the moments you doubt His wisdom in your life? What specific situation do you need to surrender to His perfect knowledge today?
?
The opposite of power is inability. This truth about God challenges your fears. Where do you still operate as if God could be powerless? What step of trust can you take right now to affirm His absolute potency?
?
Reflect on a divine attribute you rely on—mercy, justice, or will. Does your heart rest on the fact that its opposite is impossible for God? If not, what assumption about God are you holding that contradicts this lesson?

Proof of God's Remaining (Baqa')
Sanusi concludes the proof that God's remaining is as necessary as His pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for the necessity of God's remaining based on the impossibility of two equal possibilities without a preponderator.

Core Idea
God's remaining is as necessary as His pre-eternity, proven by a single logical step.

Sanusi concludes his proof for the attribute of baqa' (remaining) with a concise argument. He ties it directly to the earlier proof for qidam (pre-eternity), showing that the same logic applies to God's eternal future existence. This passage demonstrates how kalam uses the principle of the preponderator to link two essential divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the rhetorical question and the concluding phrase.
The passage is a single argument, not a list.
2
Understand the key terms
Identify the terms 'بقاء' (baqa'), 'قدم' (qidam), and 'فاعل مرجح' (preponderating agent).
These are central to the argument.
3
Follow the logical structure
The argument: if two equally possible outcomes exist without a preponderator, it's impossible. But we already proved God's pre-eternity is necessary. Therefore, His remaining must also be necessary.
4
Ask: why is this proof valid?
Consider that if God could cease to exist, then He would be contingent in the future, which contradicts the impossibility of equal possibilities without a preponderator.
This connection is what Sanusi uses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقابله المساوي له في القبولِ مِنْ غيرِ فاعل مرجح ، كيف وقد سبق قريباً بالبرهان القاطع وجوب قدمِهِ جَلَّ وعزَّ ؟! فإذاً ؛ يجبُ بقاؤُهُ تبارك وتعالى كما وجب قدمه
Its counterpart equal to it in acceptance without a preponderating agent – how [could that be] when we have already proven by decisive proof the necessity of His pre-eternity, may He be exalted and glorified?! Therefore, His remaining, blessed and exalted, is necessary as His pre-eternity was necessary.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a short argument that concludes the proof for the attribute of baqa' (remaining). The argument runs: if there were two equal possibilities without a preponderator, that would be impossible. But we have already proven that God is necessarily pre-eternal (qadim). Therefore, He cannot be contingent; He must also be eternal in the future (baqi). The conclusion is stated directly: His remaining is necessary just as His pre-eternity was necessary.

Key Terms
بقاء
قدم
فاعل مرجح
مقابله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that proving qidam automatically proves baqa' without additional reasoning.
Correction: This passage shows that baqa' requires a separate argument based on the impossibility of equality without a preponderator, not a direct consequence of qidam.

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'مقابله المساوي له في القبول من غير فاعل مرجح' refer to?
A) The impossibility of two equal possibilities existing without a preponderator
B) The necessity of God's power
C) The definition of a contingent being
D) The proof for God's unity

Key Takeaway
God's remaining (baqa') is a necessary attribute proven by the same principle of impossibility of equal possibilities without a preponderator that underlies the proof for His pre-eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
God's existence is eternally secure—never beginning, never ending. In contrast, your life is fragile and fleeting. If you truly believed this, what would change about how you spend your time today? What would you stop doing, and what would you start?
?
The proof for baqa' relies on the impossibility of equal possibilities without a preponderator. Are there areas in your life where you treat two equal choices as if they are both viable without seeking God's guidance as the decisive factor? How does this logical principle expose your spiritual negligence?
?
Since God's remaining is necessary, His promises are absolutely certain. Name one promise of God that you have doubted or failed to rely on. What does this lesson demand you do about that doubt right now?
